f ocused 	 on
composites >
In May 2011, we announced the strategic disposal of our Supply Chain 
business in a transformational move to create a focused advanced 
composites business serving high growth global end markets.
S t r o n g>s t r a t e g i c>r a t i o n a l e
Composites represent a more attractive opportunity 
with higher growth prospects, higher profit margin 
characteristics, lower working capital, and potential 
acquisition opportunities.
These prospects stem from strong market and 
structural drivers and from the benefits of using 
composite materials as an alternative to conventional 
materials due to factors such as rising energy costs 
and increasing environmental and safety concerns. 
The Composites and Supply Chain businesses  
have no material synergies and they operate with 
fundamentally different customers, processes and 
financial characteristics. We consider that each would 
benefit from independent management focus.
The proceeds of sale of the Supply Chain business will 
provide a strengthened balance sheet so that future 
growth and potential acquisition opportunities in the 
composites market can be undertaken. 3 U meco 	 p l c	 An nu a l 	 R e po r t 	 2 0 11

The advanced composites market
T h e>a d v a n c e d>c o m p o s i t e s>m a r k e t
The terms ‘advanced composites’ and ‘prepreg’ have become 
accepted as the generic names for a generation of materials 
manufactured from high performance fibres pre-impregnated with a 
suitable resin matrix. These materials are developed, manufactured 
and supplied by our Structural Materials business.
Vital to the effective processing of these materials, are the vacuum 
bagging materials which are developed, manufactured and supplied 
by our Process Materials business.
Advanced composites, prepregs and vacuum bagging materials are 
used by our customers to manufacture components, parts, structures 
and tooling designed for use in our core markets. In many cases, 
advanced composite parts and components are replacing traditional 
metallic parts and components.
A>h i g h>g r ow t h>m a r k e t
The global industry for composite materials is forecast to grow 
significantly in the coming years. The two sectors that will drive this 
growth are anticipated to be aerospace & defence and wind energy, 
where compound annual growth rates are expected to be 14 per cent 
and 8 per cent respectively.
Industry estimates show a compound growth in demand for carbon 
fibres – a key indicator in relation to the wider market for composite 
materials – of 19 per cent per annum between 2011 and 2015 followed 
by 11 per cent per annum between 2015 and 2019.
K e y>b e n e fi t s
Composites have several advantages over conventional metallic  
alloys. High strength structures can be designed, with significant 
weight savings.
Exceptional environmental degradation and corrosion   >
resistance properties. 
Damaged structures can be repaired easily. >
Ability to manufacture complex shapes at lower costs compared  >
with fabricated or machined metallic alloys. 
Time and cost reductions on tooling and manufacturing of one-offs,  >
prototypes and short length production runs. 
Excellent fatigue life, i.e. carbon fibre composites can be designed   >
to be essentially fatigue free. 
Improved energy absorbing safety structures. > 5 U meco 	 p l c	 An nu a l 	 R e po r t 	 2 0 11

Market opportunities
A e r o s p a c e>&>d e f e n c e
The growing demand for lower fuel consumption, aligned with 
advances in composite construction techniques, has led to a significant 
increase in the use of composites in civil aircraft in the last few years. 
New aircraft such as the Airbus A380XWB and the Boeing 787  
have circa 50 per cent composites compared to circa 20 per cent for 
current models. 
W i n d>e n e r g y
Previous European industry leadership in this market sector has been 
overtaken by China and we are well placed to take advantage of this 
geographical shift through our joint venture in Shanghai.
With the potential deployment of up to 29GW of additional offshore 
wind capacity by 2020, the UK is the single, largest market for offshore 
wind globally for the foreseeable future. This presents a major 
opportunity for the UK given the potential demand for bigger,  
stronger and more durable composite turbine blades. 
f ocused 	 on 	opportunity>
R e cr e ati o n
Use of composite materials, using mainly glass fibre and polyester 
resins, is long established as the main construction material for boat 
hulls, decks and superstructures in the recreational boatbuilding 
segment. A move away from open moulding to vacuum bagging is 
being accelerated by health & safety considerations.
Au to m o ti v e
As the UK moves towards a low carbon economy, more 
environmentally-friendly car designs will increasingly seek out 
lightweight materials, such as advanced composites, to cut fuel 
emissions and reduce running costs.
Industry activity and investment aimed at overcoming existing barriers 
to high volume manufacture of composite parts and components will 
influence the uptake of advanced composite materials. 6 U meco 	 p l c	 An nu a l 	 R e po r t 	 2 0 11 6 U meco 	 p l c	 An nu a l 	 R e po r t 	 2 0 11

P r o c e s s S t r u c t u r a l
A e r o s p a c e>&>D e f e n c e
We supply civil aerospace Original Equipment 
Manufacturers (“OEM”) either direct or 
through their own significant suppliers. Our 
materials are used in new builds and are 
specified by the OEM as part of long life 
assembly programmes. Our materials are 
found in secondary aircraft structures, 
interiors, bins, panels and ducting and our 
vacuum bagging materials find a wide range 
of applications spanning civil and military 
aerospace requirements. The civil aerospace 
OEM market is a long-term growth market. 
Advanced composites are widely used in the 
defence sector in areas as diverse as ballistics 
protection, fighter jet simulators and 
Unmanned Aerial Vehicles.
Customers include Boeing, Airbus,  
Martin Baker, GKN Aerospace and the 
US Navy.
W i n d>E n e r g y
The wind energy market is driven by 
regulatory pressures designed to stimulate 
electricity generation through renewable 
sources. Demand for our product primarily 
arises from the need to use advanced 
composites in turbine blades.
We have a significant share of the global 
market for vacuum bagging systems for the 
production of wind turbine blades, and we 
supply prepregs for tooling and specialist 
wind and tidal turbine blade applications.
In September 2010, we entered into a joint 
venture with our Chinese distributor Shanghai 
Leadgo Technology Co., Ltd  
with the aim of establishing a facility in 
Shanghai, China to manufacture vacuum 
bagging films for the rapidly growing Chinese 
wind energy market. This facility is expected 
to be fully operational by the end of 2011.
Customers include Vestas, L M Wind Power 
and Siemens.
R e cr e ati o n
This sector principally comprises motorsport 
and marine together with sports & leisure.
The motorsport segment is characterised by 
frequent changes in regulations, high 
demands on product performance as well as 
high service demands and an emphasis on 
safety.
Products are subject to frequent specification 
changes with annual changes in requirements 
being proposed by the teams and by changing 
rules, especially in Formula 1.
The Structural Materials business enjoys a 
significant share of the prepreg market within 
the motorsport segment.
Customers include all of the teams on the 
Formula 1 grid as well as Le Mans teams, 
lower Formulas and motorsport teams active 
in other parts of the world.

R e c r e a t i o n>conti n ued
The marine segment is influenced by the 
timing of race series such as the America’s 
Cup, resulting in periods of high market 
demand and relatively cyclical activity. 
Although the high profile racing community 
was relatively unaffected by the economic 
downturn, the wider market is recovering 
slowly after a difficult period.
We manufacture and supply prepreg and 
vacuum bagging materials across this market 
segment. We distribute glass fibre, resins and 
other materials for the general European 
marine market.
Customers include many teams participating 
in high profile events such as the America’s 
Cup and Volvo Ocean Race.
The high performance sports goods segment 
includes advanced composite materials for 
hockey sticks, the remote control hobbyist 
market, bicycles and fishing rods.
Au to m o ti v e
The superior performance and lightweight 
characteristics of advanced composite 
components and parts are having an 
increasing influence on the utilisation of 
advanced composites in the supercar and 
luxury car segments of the automotive 
market. Supercar bodies, chassis and internal 
components are typically built out of 
advanced composites. These utilise our 
prepreg and vacuum bagging films. 
Manufacturers of mid range vehicles are also 
seeking weight reduction due to European 
CO2 emissions regulations which become 
effective in 2015 and 2020.
Considerable industry activity is taking place 
to overcome manufacturing and cost 
limitations in the use of advanced composites 
and opportunities exist in the embryonic 
market for lightweight electric vehicles.
Customers include Lamborghini and 
Delta Motorsport.
 
O t h e r>I n du s t r i a l
This market sector is characterised by a diverse 
range of applications such as medical hardware, 
communications satellites, specialist food 
packaging and industrial transportation and 
construction systems.
Typically, advanced composites are used 
where low weight, combined with high 
strength and/or rigidity is required.
We manufacture and supply prepregs, vacuum 
bagging films as well as highly specialised films 
for food and other packaging applications.
Customers include Bakkersland.

Key performance indicators
Financial KPIs
Revenue, order intake and order books. • >
Operating profit and operating margin – these KPIs • >
measure the absolute value of operating profit and 
operating profit as a percentage of revenue.
Profitability – the Group’s main profitability •>
KPIs are operating profit, profit before tax, and 
earnings per share.
Operating cash flow – the cash flow from •>
operating activities is closely monitored, with 
particular focus on working capital measures 
including stock turn, debtor and creditor days, 
working capital to sales ratios and return on 
capital employed.
Non-financial KPIs
Health & safety – the safety performance of each • >
operating unit is monitored, and statistics on 
incidents and accidents are compiled, reviewed 
and reported upon. Further information on health 
& safety is contained in the Corporate Governance 
statement.
Customer service levels are monitored. • >
Employee absence and turnover rates are monitored • >
wherever relevant.
Other specific indicators, relating to production • >
efficiency and output are reported and monitored 
as required. 20 20 U meco 	 p l c	 An nu a l 	 R e po r t 	 2 0 11

C h u b b ’ s 	 h ot e l 	 sec u r it y 	 d ivi s i o n . 26 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
The Directors of Umeco (the ‘Company’) submit their Annual Report 
and financial statements for the year to 31 March 2011.
Principal activities
Umeco is an international provider of advanced composite materials 
primarily to the aerospace & defence, wind energy, recreation and 
automotive industries. Umeco is managed through two continuing 
business streams:
Umeco Composites – Structural Materials develops, manufactures  
and supplies a broad range of advanced composite materials for a 
diverse range of industries such as aerospace & defence, wind energy, 
recreation and automotive. 
Umeco Composites – Process Materials develops, manufactures and 
supplies vacuum bagging materials to the composites industry and 
other markets, providing a wide range of materials and technical 
support to a growing number of international customers. 
Disposal of Supply Chain
On 20 May 2011, the Company announced its intention to become a 
focused advanced composites business through the sale of the Supply 
Chain business. This strategic disposal will create a business focused 
on the advanced composites market, which the Board considers has 
attractive long-term growth prospects. The Supply Chain business is 
proposed to be sold to a company established by funds advised by 
Exponent Private Equity LLP for an unadjusted cash and debt free value 
of approximately £145.8 million. The net consideration in respect of 
the disposal is expected to be approximately £109.3 million (before 
transaction costs of approximately £7.4 million), of which £8.0 million 
will be deferred and paid in four equal quarterly instalments between 
29 June 2012 and 29 March 2013.
Review of Group’s business
Under Section 417 of the Companies Act 2006, the Company is 
required to produce a fair review of its business, including a description 
of the principal risks and uncertainties that face the Company. This is  
set out in the Business Review on pages 8 to 23, which includes the 
Chairman’s Statement, Chief Executive’s Review and Finance Director’s 
Review, together with descriptions of the principal activities. The 
Business Review is incorporated into this report by reference. The 
Business Review contains details of the key performance measures 
used to manage and control the Group’s operations, and sets out 
information on the future strategy and prospects of the Group.
The following specific issues are discussed in the sections shown  
in brackets:
key objectives and performance in the year to 31 March 2011 • 
(Chairman’s Statement, Chief Executive’s Review and Finance 
Director’s Review);
treasury policy and risk management (note 27 to the consolidated • 
financial statements and Corporate Governance); and
corporate social responsibility, environmental matters and • 
employee issues (Corporate Responsibility and Corporate 
Governance).
Details of the results for the year are shown in the Consolidated 
Statement of Comprehensive Income. Analyses of revenue and 
adjusted operating profit by segment are shown in note 1 to the 
consolidated financial statements.
Group key performance indicators
The Board has adopted various financial and non-financial key 
performance indicators (‘KPIs’) to measure the strategic and 
operational progress of the Group, which are measured at Group and/
or subsidiary level as appropriate. Details are shown on page 19.
Corporate governance
Under Disclosure and Transparency Rule 7.2, the Company is required  
to include a Corporate Governance statement in its Directors’ Report.  
All relevant information on the corporate governance practices of the 
Company are set out in the Corporate Governance statement on pages 
79 to 85. The Corporate Governance statement is incorporated into 
this report by reference.
Profits and dividends
The Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income is shown on 
page 33. Profit before tax from continuing operations was £8.6 million 
(2010: £6.3 million). The comparative results of the Supply Chain 
business, which was held for sale in the year, and Advanced 
Composites Group SA (Pty) Limited (‘ACG South Africa’), which was 
discontinued in the previous year have been classified as held for sale.
The Directors propose a final dividend of 11.5 pence per share, payable  
on 7 October 2011 to shareholders registered on 9 September 2011, 
making a total declared for the year to 31 March 2011 of 18.25 pence 
per share (2010: 17.5 pence).
Research & development
Expenditure on research & development was £2.1 million (2010: £2.0 
million). This expenditure relates to the research & development of 
advanced composite materials, including materials evaluation and 
prototype production. The accounting policy on research & 
development is disclosed in Group Accounting Policies.
Share capital
Details of share capital are given in note 19 to the consolidated 
financial statements. At the date of this report there were 48,140,816 
ordinary shares of 25 pence each in issue, all of which are fully paid up 
and quoted on the London Stock Exchange. 
Rights and obligations attaching to shares
The rights attaching to the Company’s ordinary shares, as well as the 
powers of the Company’s Directors, are set out in the Company’s  
Articles of Association (the “Articles”), copies of which can be obtained 
from the Company Secretary.

Subject to applicable statutes (in this section the “Companies Acts”), 
any resolution passed by the Company under the Companies Acts and 
other shareholders’ rights, shares may be issued with such rights and 
restrictions as the Company may by ordinary resolution decide, or  
(if there is no such resolution or so far as it does not make specific 
provision) as the Board (as defined in the Articles) may decide. Subject 
to the Articles, the Companies Acts and other shareholders’ rights, 
unissued shares are at the disposal of the Board.
Voting
Every member and every duly appointed proxy present at a general 
meeting or class meeting has, upon a show of hands, one vote and 
every member present in person or by proxy has, upon a poll, one  
vote for every share held by him. In the case of joint holders of a share 
the vote of the senior who tenders a vote, whether in person or by 
proxy, shall be accepted to the exclusion of the votes of the other  
joint holders and, for this purpose, seniority shall be determined  
by the order in which the names stand in the register in respect  
of the joint holding.
Restrictions on voting
No member shall be entitled to vote at any general meeting or class 
meeting in respect of any share held by him if any call or other sum 
then payable by him in respect of that share remains unpaid or if a 
member has been served with a restriction notice (as defined in  
the Articles) after failure to provide the Company with information 
concerning interests in those shares required to be provided under  
the Companies Acts. The Company is not aware of any agreements 
between holders of securities that may result in restrictions on  
voting rights.
Dividends and other distributions
The Company may by ordinary resolution from time to time declare 
dividends not exceeding the amount recommended by the Board. 
Subject to the Companies Acts, the Board may pay interim dividends, 
and also any fixed rate dividend, whenever the financial position of  
the Company, in the opinion of the Board, justifies its payment. If  
the Board acts in good faith, it is not liable to holders of shares with 
preferred or pari passu rights for losses arising from the payment of 
interim or fixed dividends on other shares. The Board may withhold 
payment of all or any part of any dividends or other moneys payable  
in respect of the Company’s shares from a person with a 0.25 per cent 
interest (as defined in the Articles) if such a person has been served 
with a restriction notice (as defined in the Articles) after failure to 
provide the Company with information concerning interests in those 
shares required to be provided under the Companies Acts.
Variation of rights
Subject to the Companies Acts, rights attached to any class of shares 
may be varied with the written consent of the holders of not less  
than three-fourths in nominal value of the issued shares of that class 
(calculated excluding any shares held as treasury shares), or with the 
sanction of a special resolution passed at a separate general meeting 
of the holders of those shares. At every such separate general meeting 
(except an adjourned meeting) the quorum shall be two persons 
holding or representing by proxy not less than one-third in nominal 
value of the issued shares of the class (calculated excluding any shares 
held as treasury shares). The rights conferred upon the holders of any 
shares shall not, unless otherwise expressly provided in the rights 
attaching to those shares, be deemed to be varied by the creation or 
issue of further shares ranking pari passu with them.
Restrictions on transfer of securities in the Company
There are no restrictions on the transfer of securities in the Company, 
except:
that certain restrictions may from time to time be imposed by laws • 
and regulations (for example, insider trading laws); and
pursuant to the Listing Rules of the Financial Services Authority • 
whereby certain employees of the Company require the approval of 
the Company to deal in the Company’s ordinary shares.
The Company is not aware of any agreements between shareholders 
that may result in restrictions on the transfers of securities and/or 
voting rights. No person holds securities in the Company carrying  
special rights with regard to control of the Company. The Articles may 
be amended by special resolution of the Company’s shareholders. 
Share allotment
A general allotment power and a limited power to allot in specific 
circumstances for cash otherwise than pro-rata to existing 
shareholders were given to the Directors by resolutions approved at 
the Annual General Meeting of the Company held on 28 July 2010. 
These powers will expire at the conclusion of the 2011 Annual General 
Meeting and resolutions to renew the Directors’ powers are therefore 
included within the notice of the 2011 Annual General Meeting.
Appointment and replacement of Directors
The Directors shall be not less than two and not more than 15 in 
number. The Company may by ordinary resolution vary the minimum 
and/or maximum number of Directors. A Director shall not be required 
to hold any shares in the Company. Directors may be appointed by the 
Company by ordinary resolution or by the Board. A Director appointed 
by the Board holds office only until the next following Annual General 
Meeting of the Company and is then eligible for re-appointment. The 
Board or any committee authorised by the Board may from time to 
time appoint one or more Directors to hold any employment or 
executive office for such period and on such terms as they may 
determine and may also revoke or terminate any such appointment.
At every Annual General Meeting of the Company any Director who has 
been appointed by the Board since the last Annual General Meeting,  
or who held office at the time of the two preceding Annual General 
Meetings and who did not retire at either of them, or who has held 
office with the Company, other than employment or executive office,  
for a continuous period of nine years or more at the date of the meeting, 
shall retire from office and may offer himself for re-appointment by the 
members. The Company may by special resolution remove any Director 
before the expiration of his period of office. The office of a Director shall 
be vacated if: (i) he resigns or offers to resign and the Board resolve to 
accept such offer; (ii) his resignation is requested by all of the other 
Directors and all of the other Directors are not less than three in number; 
(iii) he is or has been suffering from mental or physical ill health and the 
Board resolves that his office be vacated;   28 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
(iv) he is absent without the permission of the Board from meetings  
of the Board (whether or not an alternate Director appointed by him 
attends) for six consecutive months and the Board resolves that his 
office is vacated; (v) he becomes bankrupt or compounds with his 
creditors generally; (vi) he is prohibited by a law from being a Director; 
(vii) he ceases to be a Director by virtue of the Companies Acts; or (viii) 
he is removed from office pursuant to the Articles.
Powers of the Directors
Subject to the Articles, the Companies Acts and any directions given by 
the Company by special resolution, the business of the Company will 
be managed by the Board who may exercise all the powers of the 
Company, whether relating to the management of the business of the 
Company or not. In particular, the Board may exercise all the powers of 
the Company to borrow money, to guarantee, to indemnify, to 
mortgage or charge any of its undertaking, property, assets (present 
and future) and uncalled capital and to issue debentures and other 
securities and to give security for any debt, liability or obligation of the 
Company or of any third party.
Directors
The names of Directors at the date of this report, together with 
biographical details, are shown on pages 24 and 25. The remuneration of 
the Directors, together with details of their share options and share 
interests, is disclosed in the Remuneration Report on pages 86 to 93.
The appointment of a Director is a matter for resolution by the  
Board as a whole, acting through the nomination committee.  
Re-appointment is subject to review and is not automatic. Details  
of the appointment and replacement of Directors is disclosed in the 
Corporate Governance statement. Where appropriate, the nomination 
committee uses the services of external recruitment consultants. 
Details of potential candidates provided by consultants may be initially 
reviewed by a sub-committee of the nomination committee and 
meetings with selected candidates are then held with Directors. 
Subsequently, the nomination committee meets to discuss and 
confirm an appointment.
On 20 May 2011, the Company announced that Andrew Moss had 
been appointed as Chief Executive, and Steve Bowers had been 
appointed as Finance Director, in each case with immediate effect. 
Andrew Moss joined the Group in 1999. He joined the Board in June 
2008 on his appointment as Chief Operating Officer, prior to which he 
was Chief Executive of Umeco Composites. He has a broad industrial 
and aerospace background, and was previously Chief Executive of the 
Automotive and Building Products Group of Invensys plc.
Steve Bowers joined the Group in 1998 having qualified as a chartered 
accountant with KPMG. He has been Company Secretary since 1999 
and was appointed Group Financial Controller in 2004.
Directors retire by rotation at intervals of no more than three years,  
in accordance with the Combined Code.

Conflicts of interest
The Board continues to operate the procedures adopted following the 
introduction of the statutory directors’ duty to avoid conflicts of 
interest and these procedures have operated effectively during the 
year. The Articles permit the Directors to authorise conflicts of interest. 
The conflicted Director shall not count towards the quorum or vote on 
any resolution to authorise the conflict of interest and, at the Board’s 
discretion, may be excluded from any meeting at which the conflict is 
under consideration. Where a conflict of interest is authorised, the 
Board may impose such restrictions on the conflicted Director as they 
deem appropriate such as excluding the Director from receipt of 
information or discussions.

Going concern
A review of Group business activities and future outlook is set out  
on pages 8 to 23 which includes the Chairman’s Statement, Chief 
Executive’s Review and Finance Director’s Review. The financial 
position of the Group, its cash flows and liquidity position is shown in 
the Consolidated Balance Sheet and Consolidated Statement of Cash 
Flows and accompanying notes to the financial statements. The 
principal business risks associated with the business are shown on 
pages 20 to 22. In addition, note 27 to the consolidated financial 
statements includes the Group’s objectives, policies and processes for 
managing its capital, its financial risk management objectives, details 
of its financial instruments and hedging activities and its exposures to 
credit and liquidity risk.
The Group’s bank facilities with Lloyds Banking Group amount to 
£159.1 million. This comprises a US$150.0 million committed revolving 
facility which extends to June 2014, a US$89.0 million term loan facility 
which in September 2010 was extended until August 2012 and an 
overdraft of £10.0 million.
The Group has entered into an agreement for a new five-year 
committed multi currency revolving credit facility with HSBC Bank plc 
and Santander UK plc, comprising £15.0 million and US$25.0 million 
facilities. Utilisation of the facilities is conditional on, inter alia, 
completion of the disposal of the Supply Chain business and notices of 
prepayment being delivered to Lloyds Banking Group in respect of the 
facilities referred to above.
After considering the nature and duration of these facilities and 
making appropriate enquiries, based on the strength of the Group’s 
balance sheet, current expectations of future trading (based on future 
cash flow forecasts and revenue projections which the Directors 
believe are based on a realistic assessment of future business 
performance) and on the facilities available to the Group, the Directors 
believe they have reasonable grounds for stating that the Company 
and the Group have adequate resources to continue in operational 
existence for the foreseeable future. For this reason, they continue to 
adopt the going concern basis in preparing the financial statements.
Authority to make market purchases of own shares
An authority to make market purchases of shares was given to the Directors 
by a special resolution at the Annual General Meeting of the Company held 
on 28 July 2010. In the year to 31 March 2011, the Company has not 
acquired any of its own shares. The existing authority will expire at the 
conclusion of the 2011 Annual General Meeting and a resolution to renew 
the authority is therefore included within the notice of the 2011 Annual 
General Meeting.
Accordingly, it is intended to propose a Special Resolution to give the 
Company authority to make market purchases on the London Stock 
Exchange of up to 10.0 per cent of the ordinary shares in issue at the date of 
the Annual General Meeting. Any purchase therefore will be subject to the 
terms of the Listing Rules, which provide that the maximum price (exclusive 
of expenses) which may be paid for an ordinary share is the highest of (i) an 
amount equal to 5.0 per cent above the average market value for an 
ordinary share for the five business days immediately preceding the date of 
the purchase and (ii) the higher of the price of the last independent bid on 
the trading venues where the purchase is carried out.
The minimum price (exclusive of expenses) which may be paid for an 
ordinary share is 25 pence, its nominal value. Such market purchases  
of ordinary shares would be made from the Company’s distributable 
reserves. Ordinary shares purchased pursuant to the authority will either 
be cancelled or held as treasury shares. Shares held by the Company as 
treasury shares may be sold, transferred for the purpose of employee 
share schemes, or cancelled.
Related party transactions 
Related party transactions are set out in note 16 on page 78.
Essential contracts and significant agreements
The Company and Group have a number of significant agreements 
relating to funding and customer relationships. 
The Group’s facility agreements with Lloyds Banking Group in respect of 
the US$150.0 million five year revolving credit facility expiring in June 2014 
and the US$89.0 million credit facility expiring in August 2012 are essential 
to the Group as a whole. These agreements include change of control 
provisions and, in the event of a change in ownership of the Company, the 
provisions could result in renegotiation or withdrawal of the facilities. As 
announced on 20 May 2011, the proceeds of sale of the Supply Chain 
business will primarily be used towards the settlement of all outstanding 
indebtedness under these facilities, following which they will be cancelled.
The Group’s facility agreements with HSBC Bank plc and Santander 
UK plc in respect of the revolving credit bank facility, comprising £15.0 
million and US$25.0 million facilities, are essential to the Group as a 
whole. These agreements include change of control provisions and, in 
the event of a change in ownership of the Company, the provisions could 
result in cancellation of the facilities.
The Group has essential relationships with its key customers, with many 
of these relationships being the subject of long-term supply agreements. 
Other than as noted above, the Directors are not aware of any 
significant agreements to which the Company and/or any of its 
subsidiaries is a party that take effect, alter or terminate upon a  
change of control of the Company following a takeover bid.

Directors’ and officers’ liability insurance
Throughout the year to 31 March 2011, the Company maintained liability 
insurance for its Directors and officers, and the Directors and officers of 
the Group’s subsidiaries, as permitted by the Companies Acts.
Supplier payment policy
It is the Group’s normal procedure to agree payment terms with 
suppliers in advance and to adhere to those agreed terms when 
making payments. At 31 March 2011, the Company’s outstanding 
indebtedness to trade creditors corresponded to 45 days when 
averaged over the year (2010: 52 days).

Statement of Directors’ Responsibilities
The Directors are responsible for preparing the Annual Report, and  
the Group and Company financial statements, in accordance with 
applicable law and regulations.
Company law requires the Directors to prepare Group and parent 
Company financial statements for each financial year. Under that  
law, they are required to prepare the Group financial statements in 
accordance with IFRS as adopted by the EU and applicable law, and 
have elected to prepare the parent Company financial statements  
in accordance with UK Accounting Standards and applicable law  
(UK Generally Accepted Accounting Practice).
Under company law, the Directors must not approve the financial 
statements unless they are satisfied that they give a true and fair  
view of the state of affairs of the Group and parent Company and  
their profit or loss for that period. In preparing each of the Group and 
parent Company financial statements, the Directors are required to:
select suitable accounting policies and then apply them • 
consistently;
make judgements and estimates that are reasonable and prudent; • 
for the Group financial statements, state whether they have  • 
been prepared in accordance with IFRS as adopted by the EU;
for the parent Company financial statements, state whether • 
applicable UK accounting standards have been followed, subject  
to any material departures disclosed and explained in the parent 
Company financial statements; and
prepare the financial statements on a going concern basis, unless  • 
it is inappropriate to presume that the Group and the parent 
Company will continue in business.
The Directors are responsible for keeping proper accounting records 
that are sufficient to show and explain the parent Company’s 
transactions and disclose with reasonable accuracy at any time the 
financial position of the parent Company and to enable them to ensure 
that its financial statements comply with the Companies Acts. They 
have general responsibility for taking such steps as are reasonably open 
to them to safeguard the assets of the Group and to prevent and 
detect fraud and other irregularities.
The Directors confirm that they have complied with the above 
requirements in preparing the financial statements.
Under applicable law and regulations, the Directors are also 
responsible for preparing a Directors’ Report, Directors’ Remuneration 
Report and Corporate Governance statement that comply with such 
law and regulations.
The Directors are responsible for the maintenance and integrity of the 
corporate and financial information included on the Group’s website. 
Legislation in the UK governing the preparation and dissemination of 
financial statements may differ from legislation in other jurisdictions.
The Directors, namely Neil Johnson, Andrew Moss, Steve Bowers, 
Stephen Bird, Graham Zacharias, Chris Hole and Adrian Auer, confirm 
that to the best of their knowledge, the financial statements, prepared  
in accordance with IFRS as adopted by the EU, give a true and fair  
view of the assets, liabilities, financial position and income and 
expenditure of the Company (and the Group as a whole) as required  
by Disclosure and Transparency Rule 4.1.12. The Annual Report includes 
a fair review of the development and performance of the business and 
the position of the Company (and the Group as a whole), together with 
a description of the principal risks and uncertainties and a statement 
by the auditors of their responsibilities.

*Note on adjusted figures
Umeco uses adjusted figures as key performance indicators. Adjusted figures are stated before the results of discontinued operations, 
amortisation and impairment charges relating to intangible assets, significant items, the revaluation of financial instruments based on their 
market values and associated tax effects. The differences between the total and unadjusted measures of operating profit, profit before tax and 
profit attributable to owners of the Company are reconciled in note 8 to the consolidated financial statements. The narrative contained in the 
Business Review is based on the adjusted measures of operating profit, profit before tax and earnings per share. These provide a more consistent 
measure of operating performance.
The comparative figures for the year to 31 March 2010 have been re-presented to reflect the proposed disposal of the Supply Chain business.

They are prepared on the historic cost basis except that the following 
assets and liabilities are stated at their fair values – derivative financial 
instruments (IAS39), retirement benefit obligations (IAS19) and share 
based payments (IFRS2).
The accounting policies set out on pages 37 to 41 have been applied 
consistently in dealing with items which are considered material  
in relation to the Group’s financial statements.
The consolidated financial statements have been prepared by applying 
the accounting policies, presentation and basis of consolidation which 
were applied in the preparation of the Company’s consolidated 
financial statements for the year to 31 March 2010, which were 
prepared in accordance with International Financial Reporting 
Standards as adopted by the EU, except for the following accounting 
standards and interpretations which are effective for the Group from  
1 April 2010:
• IAS 27 (revised) ‘Consolidated and separate financial statements’
• IFRS 3 (revised) ‘Business combinations’
• Amendments to IAS 32 ‘Classification of rights issue’
• Annual Improvement Project to IFRS’s
The Annual Improvement Project to IFRS’s provides a vehicle for making 
non-urgent but necessary amendments to IFRS’s. Amendments to a 
number of standards have been adopted.
IAS 27 (revised) ‘Consolidated and separate financial statements’ and 
IFRS 3 (revised) ‘Business combinations’ include revisions in respect of 
accounting for acquisitions. The revisions require subsequent changes 
in the fair value of contingent consideration payable in respect of an 
acquisition to be recognised in the Consolidated Statement of 
Comprehensive Income rather than against goodwill, and require 
transaction costs attributable to an acquisition to be recognised 
immediately in the Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income. 
These changes will be applied prospectively, thus acquisitions as at 1 
April 2010 will not be effected by the change in standard. This standard 
has no impact upon profit or net assets in the year to 31 March 2011.
Amendments to IAS 32 ‘Classification of rights issue’ requires that 
rights, options or warrants to acquire a fixed number of the entity’s 
own equity instruments for a fixed amount of any currency are equity 
instruments if the entity offers the rights, options or warrants pro rata 
to all of its existing owners of the same class of its own non-derivative 
equity instruments. This standard has no impact upon profit or net 
assets in the year to 31 March 2011.
The following standards and interpretations had been endorsed by the 
EU by the year end but are not effective for the year to 31 March 2011:
•  Amendments to IFRIC 14 ‘Prepayment of a minimum funding 
requirement’
•  IFRIC 19 ‘Extinguishing financial liabilities with equity instruments’
•  Amendments to IFRS 7 ‘Improving disclosures about financial 
instruments’
•  Amendments to IAS 24 ‘Related party transactions’
Umeco plc is a company incorporated and domiciled in the UK.  
The address of the Company’s registered office is Concorde House, 
Warwick New Road, Leamington Spa, Warwickshire, CV32 5JG, United 
Kingdom. The Company is listed on the London Stock Exchange.
The consolidated financial statements of the Company for the year to  
31 March 2011 comprise the Company and its subsidiaries (together 
referred to as the ‘Group’). 
The consolidated financial statements were approved for release by 
the Board of Directors on 16 June 2011.
Statement of compliance
The Group’s financial statements as approved by the Directors have 
been prepared in accordance with International Financial Reporting 
Standards (‘IFRS’) as adopted by the EU. The Company has elected to 
prepare its parent Company financial statements in accordance with 
UK GAAP and these are shown on pages 71 to 78.
Going concern
The Group’s business activities, together with the factors likely to 
affect its future development, performance and position, the financial 
position of the Group, its cash flows, liquidity position and borrowing 
facilities are described in the Business Review. In addition, note 27 to 
the consolidated financial statements includes the Group’s objectives, 
policies and processes for managing its capital, its financial risk 
management objectives, details of its financial instruments and 
hedging activities and its exposures to credit and liquidity risk.
The Group’s bank facilities amount to £159.1 million. This comprises a 
US$150.0 million committed revolving facility which extends to June 
2014, a US$89.0 million term loan facility which in September 2010 
was extended until August 2012 and an overdraft of £10.0 million.
The Group has entered into an agreement for a new five-year 
committed multi currency revolving credit bank facility with HSBC 
Bank plc and Santander UK plc, comprising £15.0 million and US$25.0 
million facilities. Utilisation of the facilities is conditional on, inter alia, 
completion of the disposal of the Supply Chain business and notices of 
prepayment being delivered to Lloyds Banking Group in respect of the 
extended term loan facility and the revolving credit facility.
After considering the nature and duration of these facilities and 
making appropriate enquiries, based on the strength of the Group’s 
balance sheet, current expectations of future trading and on the 
facilities available to the Group, the Directors believe they have 
reasonable grounds for stating that the Company and the Group have 
adequate resources to continue in operational existence for the 
foreseeable future. For this reason, they continue to adopt the going 
concern basis in preparing the financial statements.
Basis of preparation
Comparative figures for the year to 31 March 2010 have been  
re-presented to reflect the classification of Umeco Supply Chain  
as a discontinued operation. The consolidated financial statements are 
presented in pounds sterling, the functional currency of the Company.

For the year to 31 March 2011

The Group has considered the impact of these new standards and

Consolidation
The consolidated financial statements incorporate the financial statements 
of the Company and all of its subsidiaries. Acquisitions are accounted for 
using the purchase method, when control over the operating and financial 
policies of a company has been acquired. Control exists when the Company 
has direct or indirect power to govern the financial and operating policies of 
an entity so as to obtain economic benefit from its activities. The existence 
and effect of potential voting rights that are currently exercisable or 
convertible are considered in assessing control. Consolidation of 
subsidiaries continues until that control ceases. The financial statements of 
subsidiaries used in the preparation of the consolidated financial 
statements are prepared for the same reporting period as the Company.
Transactions and balances between Group companies are eliminated  
on consolidation, and no profit before tax is recognised on sales made 
between Group companies until the products are sold to customers 
outside the Group.
Investments in jointly controlled entities
Joint ventures are those entities over whose activities the Group has joint 
control, established by contractual agreement. 
The Group’s share of joint ventures is accounted for using the proportionate 
consolidation method. The Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive 
Income and the Consolidated Balance Sheet include the Group’s share of 
the joint ventures’ income, expenses, assets and liabilities.
Divestments and assets held for sale
The results and cash flows of major lines of business that are held for 
sale have been classified as discontinued operations. Businesses that 
are divested are de-consolidated from the date on which 
control ceases.
When the carrying value of an asset will be recovered principally 
through a sale transaction expected to take place within twelve 
months of the balance sheet date rather than through continuing use, 
it is classified as held for sale and stated at the lower of carrying value 
and fair value less costs to sell.
Immediately before classification as held for sale, the assets, or 
components of a disposal group, are re-measured in accordance with 
the Group’s accounting policies. Thereafter generally the assets, or 
disposal group, are measured at the lower of their carrying amount and 
fair value less costs to sell. Any impairment loss on a disposal group is 
first allocated to goodwill, and then to remaining assets and liabilities 
on a pro rata basis, except that no loss is allocated to inventories, 
financial assets, deferred tax assets and employee benefit assets which 
continue to be measured in accordance with the Group’s accounting 
Group Accounting Policies continued
For the year to 31 March 2011
policies. Impairment losses on initial classification as held for sale and 
subsequent gains or losses on re-measurement are recognised in profit 
or loss. Gains are not recognised in excess of any cumulative 
impairment loss. 
Discontinued operations
A discontinued operation is a component of the Group’s business that 
represents a separate major line of business or geographical area of 
operations that has been disposed of or is held for sale, or is a subsidiary 
acquired exclusively with a view to resale. Classification as a discontinued 
operation occurs upon disposal or when the operation meets the criteria 
to be classified as held for sale, if earlier. When an operation is classified 
as a discontinued operation, the comparative Consolidated Statement of 
Comprehensive Income is re-presented as if the operation had been 
discontinued from the start of the comparative period.
Goodwill and intangible assets
Goodwill represents amounts arising on acquisition of subsidiaries. In 
respect of acquisitions that have been announced since 1 April 2004, 
goodwill represents the difference between the fair value of the cost  
of the acquisition (including the attributable costs of the acquisition) 
and the fair value of the net identifiable assets acquired, and is 
allocated to cash generating units. Positive goodwill is recognised as an 
asset on the balance sheet. Negative goodwill, representing the excess 
of the fair value of assets acquired above the fair value of consideration 
paid, arising on acquisitions is recognised immediately in the Consolidated 
Statement of Comprehensive Income.
In respect of acquisitions announced prior to 1 April 2004, goodwill is 
included on the basis of its deemed cost, which represents the amount 
recorded under UK GAAP on transition to IFRS.
Goodwill is stated at cost or deemed cost less any impairment losses. 
The carrying value of goodwill is reviewed for impairment at each 
balance sheet date.
Goodwill is not amortised but is reviewed for impairment at least 
annually. On disposal of a subsidiary undertaking, the attributable 
amount of goodwill is included in the determination of the profit  
or loss on disposal. 
Other intangible assets that are acquired by the Group are stated  
at cost less accumulated amortisation. Amortisation is charged  
to administrative expenses in the Consolidated Statement of 
Comprehensive Income over the estimated useful life of the asset.  
The useful life of each asset is assessed based on discussions with 
management and takes account of the differing natures of each of the 
intangible assets assessed. The useful lives of order books, customer 
relationships and contracts are between one and nine years.
Expenditure on internally generated goodwill is recognised as an 
expense in the Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income  
as incurred. 39 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
projected unit method. The charge to the Consolidated Statement  
of Comprehensive Income reflects the current service cost of such 
obligations, and where applicable, past service cost. The expected 
return on plan assets and the interest cost on scheme liabilities are 
included within financial income and expense in the Consolidated 
Statement of Comprehensive Income.
The retirement benefit obligation recognised in the Consolidated 
Balance Sheet represents the present value of the liabilities of the 
defined benefit schemes as reduced by the fair value of the assets of 
those schemes. Differences between the actual and expected returns 
on assets and experience gains and losses arising on scheme liabilities, 
together with differences arising from changes in assumptions, are 
recognised as other comprehensive income.
The Group’s contributions to the schemes are paid in accordance  
with the schemes’ rules and the recommendations of the  
schemes’ actuaries.
(b) share based payments
The fair value of options granted under share based payment schemes is 
recognised as an expense with a corresponding increase in equity. Fair 
values of options are estimated using the Black-Scholes model, taking into 
account the terms and conditions under which the options were granted. 
The fair value determined at grant date is expensed on a straight line basis 
over the vesting period, with the amount recognised as an expense being 
adjusted to reflect the actual number of options that vest except where 
forfeiture is solely due to market conditions, for example the Company’s 
share price not achieving the threshold for vesting.
Any proceeds received, net of directly attributable transaction costs, are 
credited to share capital and share premium when options are exercised.
Property, plant & equipment
Items of property, plant & equipment are stated at cost or deemed 
cost less accumulated depreciation. Cost includes expenditure that  
is directly attributable to the item of property, plant & equipment 
acquired. Assets held under lease finance arrangements are 
depreciated over the shorter of the lease term and the expected useful 
life of the asset. Depreciation is provided so as to write off the cost of 
property, plant & equipment over their estimated useful economic lives 
on a straight line basis as follows:
Freehold buildings and long leasehold 
 property improvements   50 years
Short leasehold property improvements   period of lease
Plant, machinery, fixtures & IT equipment  3–10 years
Motor vehicles   3–4 years
No depreciation is charged on freehold land. 
The residual values and useful lives of assets are reviewed annually for 
continued appropriateness and indications of impairment, and are 
adjusted if required.
Impairment
The carrying values of all non-current assets subject to amortisation 
and depreciation are reviewed for impairment when there is an 
indication that the assets might be impaired. In addition, non-current 
assets which have an indefinite useful life, including goodwill, are 
tested for impairment annually to determine whether there is any 
indication of impairment. If any indication of impairment exists, the 
asset’s recoverable amount is estimated. An impairment loss is 
recognised whenever the carrying amount of an asset or its cash 
generating unit exceeds its recoverable amount. The recoverable 
amount is the higher of fair value less costs to sell and the value in  
use. In determining the value in use, estimated future cash flows  
are discounted to their present value using a discount rate that  
reflects the time value of money and risks specific to the asset being 
assessed. Impairment losses are recognised immediately in the 
Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income and, in the case  
of goodwill, are not subsequently reversed.
Revenue
Revenue is recognised in the Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive 
Income at the fair value of consideration received or receivable. 
Recognition is made when goods or services are supplied or made 
available to customers against orders received and the significant risks 
and rewards of ownership have been transferred to the customer and 
the amount of revenue can be measured reliably.
Assessments are made in respect of Supply Chain contracts to 
determine whether the Group is acting as principal or agent. Where it is 
determined that the Group is acting as principal, revenue is recognised 
on a gross basis and includes the value of goods supplied. Where the 
Group acts as agent, the agency fee is recognised as revenue. Revenue 
excludes value added tax and other similar sales taxes.
No revenue is recognised where the recovery of the consideration is  
not probable. Revenue is stated after the deduction of discounts and 
allowances for estimated future rebates and returns. The methodology 
and assumptions used to estimate rebates and returns are monitored 
and adjusted in the light of contractual and legal obligations, historical 
trends, past experience and projected market conditions.
Significant items
Significant items are non-recurring items which are separately 
identified by virtue of their size or incidence so as to allow a better 
understanding of the underlying trading performance of the Group.
Employee benefits
(a) retirement benefit obligations
The Group operates pension schemes providing benefits based on final 
pensionable salaries and on contributions made by members. The assets 
of the schemes are held separately from those of the Group. For defined 
contribution pension schemes, amounts payable are charged to the 
Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income as they fall due.
For defined benefit pension schemes, the IAS19 cost of providing 
benefits is calculated annually by independent actuaries using the 
Overview Business Review
Financial
Statements Governance
Company
Information Directors 40 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
On disposal of an item of property, plant & equipment, the cost and 
related accumulated depreciation are removed from fixed assets and 
the net amount, less any proceeds, is taken to the Consolidated 
Statement of Comprehensive Income.
Inventories
Inventories are valued at the lower of cost (including, where applicable, 
raw materials, direct labour, other direct costs and related production 
overheads) and net realisable value. Cost is generally determined on a 
first in, first out basis. The net realisable value of inventory is assessed 
by reference to historic and expected future usage patterns, with 
provision being made for obsolete or slow moving items.
Research & development
Expenditure on research is charged to the Consolidated Statement of 
Comprehensive Income as incurred. Where development expenditure 
meets the criteria of IAS38, such expenditure will be capitalised and 
amortised over its useful life.
Interest
Interest receivable or payable is credited or charged to the 
Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income using the effective 
interest method. 
Income tax
Income tax comprises current and deferred tax. Income tax is 
recognised in the Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income 
except to the extent that it relates to items recognised directly in  
other comprehensive income, in which case it is recognised in other 
comprehensive income.
Current tax is the expected tax payable on taxable income for the year, 
using tax rates enacted or substantively enacted at the balance sheet 
date, and any adjustments to tax payable in respect of previous years.
Deferred tax is provided for in full, using the balance sheet liability 
method, providing for temporary differences between the carrying 
amounts of assets and liabilities for financial reporting purposes and 
the amounts used for tax purposes. No deferred tax is provided for  
in relation to temporary differences relating to goodwill that is not 
deductible for tax purposes and differences relating to investments  
in subsidiaries, except to the extent that they are expected to reverse  
in the foreseeable future, and the parent Company is not able to 
control the timing of the reversal of the temporary difference.
The amount of deferred tax provided is based on the expected manner 
of realisation or settlement of the assets and liabilities, using tax rates 
enacted or substantively enacted at the balance sheet date. A deferred 
tax asset is recognised only to the extent that it is probable that future 
taxable profits will be available against which the asset can be utilised. 
Deferred tax assets are reduced to the extent that it is no longer 
probable that the related tax benefit will be realised.
Group Accounting Policies continued
For the year to 31 March 2011
Leases
Where the Group enters into a lease which entails taking substantially 
all the risks and rewards of ownership of an asset, the lease is treated 
as a finance lease. The asset is capitalised and recorded within 
property, plant & equipment at the lower of the fair value at the date 
of acquisition or the present value of the minimum lease payments, 
and is depreciated over the shorter of its estimated useful life and the 
lease term. Future instalments under such leases, net of finance 
charges, are included within creditors. Rentals payable are apportioned 
between the finance element, which is charged to the Consolidated 
Statement of Comprehensive Income as interest, and the capital 
element, which reduces the outstanding obligation for future 
instalments. All other leases are operating leases and the rental 
charges are charged to the Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive 
Income on a straight line basis over the life of each lease.
Provisions
A provision is recognised on the Consolidated Balance Sheet when the 
Group has a present legal or constructive obligation as a result of a 
past event, and where it is probable that a reliably estimated outflow 
will be required to settle the obligation. 
Share capital
The share capital of the Company is recorded at the proceeds received, 
net of directly attributable issue costs. Consideration paid for shares  
in the Company in respect of share based payments are deducted  
from retained earnings. Where such shares subsequently vest in the 
employees under the terms of the Group’s share option schemes or  
are sold, any consideration received up to the value that has been 
recognised for such shares is included in retained earnings. Any excess 
consideration is credited to share premium.
Foreign currencies
Transactions in foreign currencies are recorded using the rate of 
exchange ruling at the date of the transaction. Monetary assets and 
liabilities denominated in foreign currencies at the balance sheet date 
are translated using the rate of exchange ruling at the balance sheet 
date and the gains or losses on translation are included in the profit 
attributable to owners of the Company. Goodwill and intangible assets 
relating to overseas operations are denominated in the currency of the 
foreign operations’ primary economic environment and are translated 
using the rate of exchange ruling at the balance sheet date with gains or 
losses on translation taken to other comprehensive income.
Subsidiaries account in the currency of their primary economic 
environment of operation, determined having regard to the currency 
that mainly influences revenue and expenses. Statements of 
comprehensive income and cash flows of overseas subsidiaries are 
translated into sterling at the average rate of exchange for the year.  
On consolidation, the balance sheets of overseas entities are translated 
into sterling at the rates of exchange ruling at the balance sheet date. 
Foreign exchange differences arising from the translation into sterling 
of equity interests in overseas subsidiary undertakings are treated as  
movements in the translation reserve. 41 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
The currencies which most influence the Group’s financial statements 
are the US dollar and Euro. The relevant exchange rates for these 
currencies were:

Financial instruments
Financial instruments are recognised when the Group becomes a party 
to the contractual provisions of the instrument. Financial assets are 
de-recognised when the rights to receive benefits have expired or have 
been transferred and the Group has transferred substantially all the 
risks and rewards of ownership. Financial liabilities are de-recognised 
when the obligation is extinguished. The principal financial assets and 
liabilities of the Group are as follows:
(a) trade receivables
Trade receivables are initially recognised at fair value and are then  
stated at amortised cost, net of any provision. A provision is made 
where there is evidence of a risk of non-payment, taking into account 
ageing, previous experience and general economic conditions. When  
a trade receivable is determined to be uncollectable it is written off, 
either against a provision or to the Consolidated Statement of 
Comprehensive Income.
(b) cash
Cash is carried in the Consolidated Balance Sheet at fair value. For the 
purposes of the Consolidated Statement of Cash Flows, cash comprises 
cash at bank and in hand together with bank overdrafts, as these items 
are an integral part of the Group’s cash management. The Group does 
not have any short-term deposit instruments.
(c) trade payables
Trade payables are initially recognised at fair value and are then stated 
at amortised cost.
(d) bank loans & other borrowings
Interest bearing bank loans and overdrafts are initially recognised  
at fair value less attributable transaction costs. All borrowings are 
subsequently stated at amortised cost with the difference between  
the initial proceeds and the repayment value being recognised in the 
Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income over the period  
to repayment.
(e) derivative financial instruments
The Group uses derivative financial instruments to manage  
financial risks associated with the Group’s business activities and the 
financing of those activities. Derivatives are initially recognised at fair 
value on the date that the contract is entered into and subsequently 
re-measured in future periods at their fair value, with any change  
in value being recognised in the Consolidated Statement of 
Comprehensive Income. The Group does not apply hedge accounting  
in respect of these financial instruments.
The Group enters into forward foreign exchange contracts to provide a 
hedge against foreign currency exposures. Interest rate swap contracts 
are used to hedge the Group’s exposure to changes in interest rates.
Fair values are based on market prices at the balance sheet date.
The Group does not hold or issue derivative financial instruments  
for speculative purposes.
(f) hedge of net investment in foreign operation
Where a foreign currency liability is a formally designated hedge of a  
net investment in a foreign operation, foreign exchange differences 
arising on translation of the foreign currency liability are recognised 
directly in equity to the extent the hedge is effective. The Group  
assesses the effectiveness of its net investment hedge based on fair  
value changes of its net assets, including relevant goodwill designated  
as a foreign currency asset and the fair value changes of the debt 
designated as a hedge.
At the inception of a hedging transaction the Group documents the 
relationship between the hedged item and the hedging instrument 
together with its risk management objective and the strategy 
underlying the proposed transaction. The Group also documents its 
assessment, both at the inception of the hedging relationship and 
subsequently on an ongoing basis, of the effectiveness of the hedge.

10 Intangible assets continued
Goodwill is allocated to cash generating units or groups of cash generating units expected to benefit from the synergies of the business 
combination. Cash generating units are normally considered to be individual businesses within the Group. Each unit or group of units to which 
the goodwill is allocated represents the lowest level within the Group at which goodwill is monitored for internal management purposes. 
Goodwill has been allocated to cash generating units or groups of cash generating units as shown in the table below.
       2011 2010 
       £m £m
Umeco Composites – Structural Materials
ACG       39.7 39.7
JD Lincoln       20.7 21.6
Umeco Composites – Process Materials 
Aerovac, Richmond, IPM and Shanghai Umeco Composites Co., Limited (‘Shanghai Umeco Composites’)  37.7 38.7
Umeco Supply Chain 
Pattonair Italy       – 12.2
Pattonair North America       – 10.7
Pattonair France       – 1.5
       98.1 124.4
Continuing operations
Each year, or whenever events or a change in the economic environment indicates a risk of impairment, the Group reviews the value of  
goodwill balances allocated to its cash generating units. Tests are performed based on internal valuations of each cash generating unit. The 
recoverable amount of goodwill attaching to cash generating units is based on value in use calculations using discounted cash flows. Those 
calculations are based on cash flow forecasts derived from the most recent forecast for the year to 31 March 2012 (2010: year to 31 March 2011) 
approved by management and strategic plans for the subsequent two years. These forecasts provide cash flow projections covering the three 
year period ending on 31 March 2014 (2010: 31 March 2013). In order to produce projections for a 25 year horizon period, the cash flow forecast 
for the year to 31 March 2014 (2010: year to 31 March 2013) was then extrapolated for a further 22 years, using growth rates appropriate to each 
cash generating unit. For the calculation of discounted cash flows made as at 31 March 2011, a terminal value was included in respect of forecast 
cash flows arising after the end of the 25 year horizon period. The following growth rates were used to derive the forecast for the year to 31 
March 2015 (2010: year to 31 March 2014) and to derive the forecast for subsequent years:
       2011 2010 
       Per cent Per cent
Umeco Composites – Structural Materials
Years four to ten       2.0-7.0 2.0-7.0
Years 11 to 25       2.0 2.0
Umeco Composites – Process Materials
Years four to ten       2.0-7.0 2.0-7.0
Years 11 to 25       2.0 2.0
These growth rates are considered to be consistent with the long-term average growth rates for the industries which the cash generating  
units serve. Growth rates are considered separately for each cash generating unit and are benchmarked against externally prepared industry 
growth projections. Management believe that the forecast period is appropriate given the long-term nature of the build programmes within  
the relevant industries.
The key assumptions for the value in use calculations are those regarding the discount rates, growth rates, achievement of future revenues and 
expected changes in direct costs during the period. These assumptions have been reviewed in light of the current economic environment which  
has resulted in a more conservative estimate about the future.
Discount rates have been estimated based on pre-tax rates that reflect the current market assessment of the time value of money and the risks specific to 
the cash generating units. Whilst the Group has a number of cash generating units, the risks and rewards associated with Umeco Composites’ operations 
are consistent and therefore the same market risk premium has been applied for these cash generating units.
Overview Business Review
Financial
Statements Governance
Company
Information Directors 52 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
10 Intangible assets continued
In cash generating units within Umeco Composites – Structural Materials, a pre-tax discount rate of between 12.3 per cent and 15.8 per cent  
has been applied in determining the recoverable amounts of cash generating units (2010: between 12.6 per cent and 16.6 per cent). For cash 
generating units within Umeco Composites – Process Materials, a pre-tax discount rate of between 9.6 per cent and 13.6 per cent has been 
applied (2010: between 12.3 per cent and 13.8 per cent). The discount rates are estimated based on the Group’s weighted average cost of capital, 
using the capital asset pricing model to determine the cost of equity and then weighting the overall cost of capital for the Group by equity and 
debt. In calculating the cost of equity a market risk premium was used with a Beta value of 0.9 (2010: 0.9). A market premium of 5.0 per cent 
(2010: 5.0 per cent) was used to calculate a pre-tax discount rate reflecting market information and risk. 
Management believe that the calculations and assumptions on which the carrying value of goodwill is based are appropriate and any reasonable 
change in the assumptions would not lead to a materially different conclusion. The Group’s estimate of impairments is most sensitive to 
increases in the discount rate used and reductions in forecast cash flows. Sensitivity analysis has been carried out in relation to the discount rate 
assumption, which demonstrated that 3.1 per cent would need to be added to the pre-tax discount rate used for Umeco Composites – Structural 
Materials, and 2.7 per cent added to the pre-tax discount rate used for Umeco Composites – Process Materials before any impairment would 
exist. Management do not consider such an increase in discount rates to be likely.
Although cash forecasts into perpetuity have been considered, the impairment tests at 31 March 2011 show that for Umeco Composites – 
Structural Materials, the number of years required to recover the carrying value of goodwill ranged from two to 11 (2010: two to 18 years). The 
equivalent period for Umeco Composites – Process Materials was five years (2010: nine years). Management consider that these payback periods 
are not excessive given the long-term strategic benefits arising from the acquisitions that have given rise to goodwill.
There were no impairments recognised in the year to 31 March 2011. Cumulative impairment recognised in relation to goodwill is £0.8 million  
(2010: £0.8 million).
The Group made no acquisitions in the years to 31 March 2011 or 31 March 2010.
Discontinued operations
During the year the Group announced the proposed disposal of Umeco Supply Chain and therefore its goodwill has been classified as held  
for sale, as shown in note 22. An impairment of £12.5 million has been recognised on this goodwill as a result of reclassifying it as a held for  
sale asset.
In the prior year, growth rates of zero to 7.0 per cent in years four to ten and 2.0 per cent from years 11 to 25 were applied in testing for impairment 
of the goodwill balance. A pre-tax discount rate of between 8.1 per cent and 14.7 per cent was used to determine its recoverable amount. The 
impairment test showed that the number of years required to recover the carrying value of goodwill ranged from one to 13 years.

On 23 March 2011 the Chancellor announced the reduction in the main rate of UK corporation tax to 26.0 per cent with effect from 1 April 2011. 
This change became substantively enacted on 29 March 2011 and therefore the effect of the rate reduction creates a reduction in the deferred 
tax liability which has been included in the figures above.
The Chancellor also proposed changes to further reduce the main rate of corporation tax by one per cent per annum to 23.0 per cent by 1 April 
2014, but these changes have not yet been substantively enacted and therefore are not included in the figures above.  The overall effect of the 
further reductions from 26.0 per cent to 23.0 per cent will be to reduce the deferred tax liability in future years.
Unrecognised deferred tax assets 
Deferred tax assets have not been recognised on tax losses of £nil (2010: £1.2 million), which relates entirely to the Supply Chain business due to 
the lack of certainty concerning the quantum and timing of future years’ taxable profits of the companies concerned.

20 Reserves
The translation reserve comprises all foreign exchange differences arising from the translation of the financial statements of foreign operations 
and the effective portion of the cumulative net change in fair value of hedging instruments. Retained earnings include the cost of the Company’s 
shares which have been acquired under the terms of deferred share awards made under the Umeco Bonus Plan and which are registered in the 
names of the award holders. Details of these awards are set out in note 26. At 31 March 2011, the reserve for own shares within retained 
earnings was £nil (2010: £0.2 million) as a result of the deferred share awards made in June 2008 and June 2009. Share premium represents the 
excess paid over the nominal value for each share.

22 Discontinued operations
On 20 May 2011, the Group announced the proposed disposal of the Supply Chain business to a company established by funds advised  
by Exponent Private Equity LLP, for a cash consideration of £145.8 million. The net consideration in respect of the disposal is expected t 
o be approximately £109.3 million. The disposal is expected to be completed in July 2011. The Supply Chain business was not a discontinued  
operation or classified as held for sale at 31 March 2010 and the results and cash flow for the comparative period have been re-presented  
to show the discontinued operation separately from continuing operations. The Supply Chain business is treated as held for sale at  
31 March 2011 in line with IFRS5 as management consider the disposal to be highly probable.
The following subsidiaries of Umeco plc, together with their place of operation and country of incorporation, form the Supply Chain business and

Off-balance sheet arrangements
In compliance with current reporting requirements, certain arrangements entered into by the Group in its normal course of business are not 
reported in the Consolidated Balance Sheet. Of such arrangements, those considered material by the Directors are trade receivable balances that 
have been subject to non-recourse factoring arrangements. 
Under its non-recourse factoring arrangements, the Group sells trade receivable balances to a third-party factoring company in exchange  
for a cash payment from the factoring company, net of fees. All the risks and rewards of the trade receivables subject to these arrangements  
are transferred to the factoring company and, accordingly, the trade receivables are derecognised in the Consolidated Balance Sheet. Such 
arrangements are used from time to time by the Group to manage the recovery of cash from its trade receivables. As at 31 March 2011, the 
Consolidated Balance Sheet included £18.4 million (2010: £17.3 million) of cash that would otherwise have been reported as trade receivables  
if these arrangements were not in place, all of which relates to Umeco Supply Chain. Factoring fees incurred during the year to 31 March 2011, 
which are written off to the Consolidated Statement of Comprehensive Income within ordinary finance costs, amounted to £0.3 million  
(2010: £0.1 million).
