24 Retirement benefit obligation
As explained in the Group Accounting Policies, the Group operates several pension schemes, the details of which are disclosed in this note.
The Umeco Pension and Life Assurance Plan (‘the Umeco Scheme’) has two sections. The defined benefit section of the Umeco Scheme, which 
was closed to new entrants in 2000, provides benefits based on final pensionable pay with contributions being charged to the Consolidated 
Statement of Comprehensive Income so as to spread the cost of pensions over employees’ working lives with the Group. The contributions are 
determined by a qualified independent actuary on the basis of valuations, conducted at least every three years, using the attained age method. 
Contribution rates are determined on the basis of advice from an independent professionally qualified actuary, with the objective of providing 
the funds required to meet pension obligations as they fall due. The most recent valuation was at 1 April 2007. The assumptions which have the 
most significant effects on the results of the valuation are those relating to the rate of return on investments before retirement (6.7 per cent per 
annum), the rate of return on investments after retirement (5.2 per cent per annum), the rate of increase in salaries (4.5 per cent per annum) and 
the rate of pensions increases (0.0–3.2 per cent per annum). The valuation adopted the PMA92 and PFA92 year of birth medium cohort tables as 
the basis for determining members’ mortality assumptions. The valuation showed that the actuarial value of the defined benefit section’s assets 
was £8.1 million which represented 77.5 per cent of the actuarial value of benefits that had accrued to members after allowing for expected 
future increases in earnings. 
Regular contributions of the Group during the year were 26.3 per cent of earnings. Regular contributions of employees ranged from 4.5 per cent  
to 6.5 per cent of earnings. Regular contributions payable in respect of the year were £0.2 million (2010: £0.3 million). As part of the deficit 
recovery plan agreed with the trustees of the Umeco Scheme, additional contributions of £0.9 million (2010: £0.9 million) were payable. On 
completion of the disposal of the Supply Chain business the Company will pay £0.7 million to reduce the deficit. Total contributions outstanding 
at the year end were £0.5 million (2010: £0.6 million). The next actuarial valuation is due as at 1 April 2010. In the year to 31 March 2012, the Group 
expects to pay regular contributions of approximately £0.2 million, representing 26.3 per cent of pensionable salaries, additional contributions of 
£0.9 million and a special lump sum contribution of £0.7 million payable within 60 days of completion of the disposal of the Supply Chain business.
The Umeco Scheme also has a defined contribution section. Members of this section contribute between 2.0 per cent and 6.0 per cent of pensionable 
earnings with the Group making contributions of between 4.0 per cent and 10.0 per cent. Contributions amounting to £0.6 million (2010: £0.4 million) 
were payable to this section of the Umeco Scheme in the year, of which £23,000 (2010: £21,000) was outstanding at the year end.
The trustees of the Umeco Scheme are chaired by John Harper, formerly one of the Company’s Non-executive Directors, and an independent 
expert in pension matters attends meetings of the trustees. Responsibility for investment of the Umeco Scheme’s funds has been delegated  
by the trustees to professional investment managers.
The Advanced Composites Group of companies participate in the Advanced Composites Group Pension Scheme (‘the ACG Scheme’), which 
provides benefits on a defined benefit basis. The ACG Scheme was closed to new entrants in 2001. The assets of the ACG Scheme are held 
separately from those of the Group and responsibility for investment of the ACG Scheme’s funds has been delegated by the trustees to 
professional investment managers. Contribution rates are determined on the basis of advice from an independent professionally qualified 
actuary, with the objective of providing the funds required to meet pension obligations as they fall due. The trustees of the ACG Scheme are 
chaired by Jon Mabbitt, Group Managing Director of Umeco Composites – Structural Materials, and an independent expert in pension matters 
attends meetings of the trustees.
Contributions to the ACG Scheme are determined by a qualified independent actuary on the basis of valuations, conducted at least every three 
years, using the projected unit method. The most recent valuation was as at 1 June 2008. The assumptions which have the most significant 
effects on the results of the valuation are those relating to the rate of return on investments before retirement (7.2 per cent per annum), the rate 
of return after retirement (5.45 per cent per annum), the rate of increase in salaries (4.8 per cent per annum) and the rate of pension increases 
(3.8 per cent per annum). The valuation adopted the PMA92 and PFA92 year of birth medium cohort tables as the basis for determining members’ 
mortality assumptions. The valuation showed that the actuarial value of the ACG Scheme’s assets was £6.9 million which represented 83.6 per 
cent of the actuarial value of benefits that had accrued to members after allowing for expected future increases in earnings. The contributions  
of the Group and employees are 15.7 per cent and 8.7 per cent of earnings respectively. Regular contributions payable in respect of the year were 
£0.3 million (2010: £0.3 million). As part of the deficit recovery plan agreed with the trustees of the ACG Scheme, additional contributions of  
£0.4 million (2010: £0.4 million) were made. Total contributions outstanding at the year end were £25,000 (2010: £52,000). The next actuarial 
valuation is due as at 1 June 2011. In the year to 31 March 2012, the Group expects to pay regular contributions of approximately £0.3 million, 
representing 15.7 per cent of pensionable salaries, and additional contributions of approximately £0.4 million.
Certain of the Group’s UK businesses operate separate defined contribution arrangements for qualifying employees. Employer contributions are  
a maximum of 10.0 per cent and employees are encouraged to contribute at similar rates. Total contributions of £0.6 million (2010: £0.4 million) 
were payable in respect of the year.

As described in the Remuneration Report, the Company makes payments to defined contribution arrangements in respect of the Executive

an independent SIPP arrangement, £nil of which was outstanding at the year end (2010: £2,000). The remaining pension contribution entitlement 
of £2,000 was converted to additional salary at Andrew Moss’ request. Details of this conversion are set out in the Remuneration Report.
IAS19
The information required for accounting in accordance with the requirements of IAS19 has been obtained by updating the actuarial valuations 
referred to above, which were carried out by independent qualified actuaries. Combined values are shown for the Umeco Scheme and the  
ACG Scheme.
The assumptions used to calculate scheme liabilities are as follows:
       2011 2010 
       Per cent Per cent
Rate of increase in pensionable salaries       4.3 4.6
Rate of increase of pensions in payment – RPI      3.5 3.6
Rate of increase of pensions in payment – CPI      3.0 –
Discount rate       5.4 5.5
Inflation       3.5 3.6
The mortality basis used for these disclosures is in line with the basis used by the respective trustees at the most recent valuations, adjusted to 
reflect members’ dates of birth.
The mortality assumptions imply the following expected future lifetimes from age 65:
         2011 2010 
       Years Years
Males currently aged 65        22.4 22.1
Females currently aged 65        24.8 25.0 
Males currently aged 45        24.3 23.1
Females currently aged 45        26.7 25.9
The assumptions have been chosen by the Directors from a range of possible actuarial assumptions which, due to the timescales covered, may 
not be borne out in practice.
The market values of the schemes’ assets, which are not intended to be realised in the short-term, may be subject to significant change before 
they are realised. The present values of the schemes’ liabilities are calculated by reference to the investment return on corporate bonds. The 
assumptions used do not necessarily represent the investment return that may be achieved.

27 Financial risk management and financial instruments
(a) financial risk management
Financial risk management is an integral part of the way the Group is managed. The Directors review and agree the broad policies for all 
significant areas of financial management. In the course of its business, the Group is exposed to foreign exchange risk, interest rate risk, liquidity 
risk and credit risk. The aim of the Group’s financial risk management policies is to minimise potential adverse effects on financial performance 
and net assets. The Group does not enter into speculative transactions.
(b) capital risk management
The Group’s objectives when managing capital are to safeguard its ability to continue as a going concern in order to provide returns  
for shareholders and for other stakeholders and to maintain an optimal capital structure. The Group considers capital to be £245.9 million  
(2010: £258.0 million), being the sum of equity attributable to owners of the Company and net debt.

27 Financial risk management and financial instruments continued
The Group monitors capital on the basis of the ratio of net debt to earnings before interest, tax, depreciation and amortisation (‘EBITDA’) and 
interest cover. These measures are the principal financial covenants under the terms of the Group’s committed facilities with Lloyds Banking 
Group. The calculation of the net debt to EBITDA covenant involves the translation of both net debt and EBITDA at the average exchange rates  
for the period. For the purposes of these facilities, the value of these measures was as follows:
       2011 2010
Net debt to EBITDA  
Ratio of net debt to EBITDA       2.08 times 2.14 times

Interest cover  
Ratio of interest to profit before interest       5.78 times 4.97 times
Covenant – ratio of interest to profit before interest not to be less than    4.00 times 4.00 times
(c) market risk – foreign currency risk and exposure
The Group puts in place forward foreign exchange contracts where it is thought necessary to use such instruments to manage the exposure  
to foreign exchange movements. At 31 March 2011, the Group had 29 forward currency contracts outstanding (2010: 32 contracts) which had  
a total principal value of £6.0 million (2010: £4.6 million).
The principal foreign currencies in which the Group transacts and holds assets and liabilities are the US dollar and the Euro. A change in value of 
the US dollar resulting in a 5.0 per cent rise in the sterling: US dollar exchange rate would result in a decrease of £0.1 million (2010: £0.2 million 
decrease) in reported profit after tax and a reduction of £1.2 million (2010: £1.6 million reduction) in net assets. A change in value of the Euro 
resulting in a 5.0 per cent rise in the sterling: Euro exchange rate would result in a reduction of £0.1 million (2010: £nil) in reported profit before 
tax and a reduction of £0.6 million (2010: £0.5 million reduction) in net assets.
The carrying amount of the Group’s borrowings denominated in foreign currencies is as follows:
       2011 2010 
       £m £m
US dollar       79.7 75.0
Euro       2.3 33.5
       82.0 108.5
Of the total foreign currency borrowing of £82.0 million (2010: £108.5 million), the amount of borrowing used for hedging the currency risk on 
retranslating overseas operations amounted to £77.0 million (2010: £81.4 million). The foreign exchange gain of £0.5 million (2010: £1.0 million) 
has been recognised in the translation reserve and in Other Comprehensive Income.
(d) market risk – interest rate risk
The Group is exposed to interest rate risk on both interest bearing assets and interest bearing liabilities. The effects of changes in interest rates 
could affect the Group’s future cash flows or the fair values of its financial instruments. It is the Group’s policy to maintain an appropriate balance 
between fixed and floating interest rates on borrowings in order to provide certainty as to the level of interest expense in the short-term and to 
reduce the impact of interest rate fluctuations over the medium term. Interest rate risk arises on floating rate debt, which comprises bank loans, 
on which interest is based on LIBOR, and cash at bank and overdrafts, on which interest is related to bank base rates.
The Group uses interest rate swap contracts to hedge the Group’s exposure to movements in interest rates. At 31 March 2011, the Group had  
one such contract outstanding (2010: one contract). The notional amount of debt covered by the interest rate swap contract was £46.8 million 
(2010: £49.4 million). At 31 March 2011, the effective interest rate on the Group’s bank loans was 3.4 per cent (2010: 3.3 per cent) and the 
effective interest rate on lease finance obligations was 6.4 per cent (2010: 5.4 per cent).
A one percentage point rise in interest rates in respect of US dollar denominated borrowings would increase the annual financial expense charge 
by approximately £0.8 million (2010: £0.9 million), however the effect of the Group’s interest rate swap contracts would reduce this impact and 
would lead to a net increase of £0.5 million (2010: £0.2 million). A similar rise in respect of sterling denominated borrowings would increase the 
annual financial expense charge by approximately £0.4 million (2010: £0.5 million).
Notes to the Consolidated Financial Statements continued
For the year to 31 March 2011 67 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
27 Financial risk management and financial instruments continued
(e) liquidity risk
Liquidity risk is the risk that the Group will not be able to meet its financial obligations as they fall due. The Group’s policy on liquidity risk is to 
ensure that sufficient cash and undrawn committed facilities are available to fund ongoing operations and to meet its medium term capital  
and funding obligations, and to meet any unforeseen obligations and opportunities.
Management monitor liquidity in terms of meeting the banking covenants described in note 27(b). The committed borrowing facilities available 
to the Group are reviewed regularly and are designed to exceed forecast peak gross debt levels. At 31 March 2011, the principal borrowing 
facilities available to the Group comprised a US$150.0 million revolving credit facility due for repayment in June 2014, a US$89.0 million term  
loan facility due for repayment in August 2012 and a £10.0 million overdraft facility that is renewable annually.
(f) credit risk
Credit risk arises on financial instruments such as trade receivables and derivative financial instruments. Policies and procedures exist to ensure 
that customers have an appropriate level of credit according to their trading history. Derivative financial instruments are executed only with 
highly credit-rated authorised counterparties based on ratings issued by the major rating agencies.
Trade & other receivables included in the Consolidated Balance Sheet are stated net of a provision for impairment which has been estimated by 
management following a review of individual receivable accounts and is based on prior experience and known factors at the balance sheet date. 
Receivables are written off against the provision when management consider that the debt is no longer recoverable. Details of changes in the 
provision are set out in note 14. For all financial instruments that are not impaired, a full recovery of their value is expected.
There are no indications as at 31 March 2011 that debtors will not meet their payment obligations in respect of the amount of trade receivables 
recognised in the Consolidated Balance Sheet that have not been provided for. For continuing operations there are £7.5 million (2010: £5.8 million) of 
trade receivables that are past due at 31 March 2011 that have not been provided against. While uncertainty surrounding counterparty risk has increased 
due to the current economic climate, the Group considers that debtors will meet their payment obligations in respect of trade receivables recognised in 
the Consolidated Balance Sheet that are past due and unprovided as at 31 March 2011. The Group considers that it has minimised its exposure to a 
significant amount of credit risk.
The continuing Group’s largest customer accounted for 3.3 per cent (2010: 1.7 per cent) of net sales from continuing operations.

28 Accounting estimates and judgements
The key assumptions concerning the future and other key sources of estimation uncertainty at the balance sheet date that have a significant risk  
of causing a material adjustment to the carrying amounts of assets and liabilities within the next financial year are as follows:
Defined benefit pension scheme valuations
In determining the valuation of defined benefit pension scheme assets and liabilities, a number of assumptions have been made, notably in 
relation to the expected return on plan assets, inflation and discount rates, mortality, salary increases and pension increases. These assumptions 
are largely dependent upon factors outside the Group’s control. Details of these assumptions are set out in note 24.
Impairment of goodwill
The determination of whether goodwill is impaired requires the conducting of an impairment test. Such tests involve an estimation of the future cash 
flows expected to be derived from the cash generating unit to which the goodwill is attached, discounted using appropriate interest rates. These cash 
flows are dependent upon future trading performance, which in turn are partially dependent upon prevailing market and economic conditions that are 
outside the Group’s control. The impairment tests are therefore inherently judgemental and future events could cause the assumptions used in the 
impairment tests to change, with a consequent adverse effect on the future results of the Group. Details of impairment testing are set out in note 10.

28 Accounting estimates and judgements continued
Disposal of Supply Chain business
In accordance with IFRS5, the Supply Chain division of Umeco has been re-presented as held for sale. At 31 March 2011, the disposal group was 
deemed available for immediate sale in its current condition and the sale was highly probable, evidenced by the announcement made in February 
2011 regarding management’s intention to sell the disposal group and the sale announcement on 20 May 2011. On re-presentation as held for 
sale, the disposal Group was measured at the lower of its carrying amount and fair value less costs to sell. Management identified the fair value 
of the disposal Group to be £5.1 million less than its carrying amount and, along with costs to sell of £7.4 million, resulted in a loss on 
re-measurement of £12.5 million.
Valuation of inventories
The Group has a formal policy for making appropriate reserves to ensure inventories are stated at the lower of cost and net realisable value. This 
policy requires assumptions to be made regarding future demand levels and these assumptions are partly dependent upon prevailing market and 
economic conditions, which are outside the Group’s control.
Valuation of intangible assets
A review is conducted in respect of each acquisition made by the Group to identify separable intangible assets. These may include customer 
relationships, contracts or orders on hand and product qualifications or approvals. The valuation of these assets is set out in note 10.
Provisions
The carrying value of the disposal provision is assessed at each balance sheet date based upon the latest available information in relation to 
expected future outflows regarding the environmental issues referred to in note 18. This information includes reports from the Group’s 
environmental consultants.

Accounting policies
The following accounting policies have been applied consistently in 
dealing with items which are considered material in relation to the 
Company’s financial statements.
Basis of preparation
The financial statements have been prepared in accordance with 
applicable UK accounting standards and law and under historical cost 
accounting rules, except for derivative financial instruments which  
are stated at their fair values. A cash flow statement has not been 
presented as permitted by FRS1 (revised) ‘Cash Flow Statements’.  
The Company has taken advantage of the exemptions contained in 
FRS8 ‘Related Party Disclosures’ and has not disclosed transactions  
or balances with entities which form part of the Group. 
Investments
Fixed asset investments in subsidiary undertakings are stated at cost, 
less provision for any impairment.
Depreciation
Depreciation is provided so as to write off the cost or valuation of 
tangible fixed assets over their estimated useful economic lives on a 
straight line basis as follows:
Freehold buildings   50 years
Plant, machinery, fixtures & IT equipment  3-10 years
Motor vehicles   3-4 years
No depreciation is charged on freehold land.
Tax
The charge for tax is based on the profit for the year and takes into 
account tax deferred because of timing differences between the 
treatment of certain items for tax and accounting purposes except as 
otherwise required by FRS19 ‘Deferred Tax’. Liabilities are calculated on a 
non-discounted full provision basis. Assets are recognised on the same 
basis, but only to the extent that it is probable they will be recovered.
Foreign currencies
Transactions in foreign currencies are recorded using the rate of 
exchange ruling at the date of the transaction. Monetary assets and 
liabilities denominated in foreign currencies are translated using the 
rate of exchange ruling at the balance sheet date and the gains or 
losses on translation are included in the profit and loss account.
Financial instruments
The Company has adopted the requirements of FRS29 ‘Financial 
Instruments: Disclosures’ and has taken the exemption under that 
standard from disclosure on the grounds that the Group’s financial 
statements contain disclosures in compliance with IFRS7 ‘Financial 
Instruments: Disclosures’. The Company does not hold or issue 
derivative financial instruments for trading purposes and the principal 
financial instruments utilised by the Company are interest rate swaps. 
These instruments are used for managing interest rate exposures in 
line with the Group’s risk management policy. 
(a) bank loans & other borrowings
Interest bearing bank loans and overdrafts are initially recognised  
at fair value less attributable transaction costs. All borrowings are 
subsequently stated at amortised cost with the difference between 
the initial proceeds and the repayment value being recognised in the 
profit and loss account over the period to repayment.
(b) derivative financial instruments
The Company uses derivative financial instruments to manage  
financial risks associated with the Company’s business activities  
and the financing of those activities. Derivatives are initially  
recognised at fair value on the date that the contract is entered into  
and subsequently re-measured in future periods at their fair value,  
with any change in value being recognised in the profit and loss 
account. The Company does not apply hedge accounting in respect  
of these financial instruments.
The Company enters into forward foreign exchange contracts to 
provide a hedge against foreign currency exposures. Interest rate swap 
contracts are used to hedge the Company’s exposure to changes in 
interest rates.
Fair values are based on quoted market prices at the balance sheet date.
(c) fair value hedge
Foreign currency borrowings (the hedging instrument) are treated as a 
fair value hedge against foreign currency investments (the hedged 
item). The hedging instrument is measured at fair value with changes 
in the fair value recognised in the profit and loss account. The hedged 
item is also re-measured with any change in the carrying value also 
being recognised in the profit and loss account.
Provisions
A provision is recognised on the Company Balance Sheet when the 
Company has a present legal or constructive obligation as a result of a 
past event, and where it is probable that an outflow will be required to 
settle the obligation.
Impairment
The carrying values of investments are reviewed at each balance sheet 
date to determine whether there is any indication of impairment. If any 
such indication exists, the asset’s recoverable amount is estimated. An 
impairment loss is recognised whenever the carrying amount of an 
asset or its cash generating unit exceeds its recoverable amount. The 
recoverable amount is the higher of fair value less costs to sell and the 
value in use. In determining the value in use, estimated future cash 
flows are discounted to their present value using a discount rate that 
reflects the time value of money and risks specific to the asset being 
assessed. Impairment losses are recognised immediately in the profit 
and loss account and are not subsequently reversed.
Company Accounting Policies
For the year to 31 March 2011 73 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
Retirement benefit obligation
Pension costs are recognised in the financial statements in accordance 
with the requirements of FRS17 ‘Retirement Benefits’. The Company  
is a member of the defined benefit section of the Umeco Scheme. 
Since the Company is unable to identify its share of the scheme assets 
and liabilities on a consistent and reasonable basis, the scheme is 
accounted for by the Company as if it was a defined contribution 
scheme. Details of the Group’s pension schemes are set out in note 24 
to the consolidated financial statements.
For defined contribution schemes, amounts payable by the Company 
are charged to the profit and loss account as they fall due.
Share based payments
The fair value of options granted after 7 November 2002 and not yet 
vested by 31 March 2004 are not recognised as an employee expense. 
Those granted since 1 April 2004 are expensed with a corresponding 
increase in equity. The fair value is measured at grant date and spread 
over the period during which the employees become unconditionally 
entitled to the options. The fair value of the options granted is 
measured using the Black-Scholes model, taking into account the terms 
and conditions upon which the options were granted. The amount 
recognised as an expense is adjusted to reflect the actual number  
of share options that vest except where forfeiture is only due to  
share prices not achieving the threshold for vesting. Details of the 
Company’s share option schemes are set out in note 26 to the 
consolidated financial statements.
Where the Company grants options over its own shares to the 
employees of its subsidiaries, it recognises an increase in the cost of 
investment in its subsidiaries equivalent to the equity settled share 
based payment charge recognised in its subsidiary’s financial 
statements with the corresponding credit being recognised directly  
in equity. Amounts recharged to the subsidiaries are recognised as  
a reduction in the cost of investment in that subsidiary.

1 Profit for the year
As permitted by Section 408 of the Companies Act 2006, the Company has elected not to present its own profit and loss account for the year.  
The Company reported a profit for the year to 31 March 2011 of £1.2 million (2010: £14.7 million). 
Fees payable to KPMG Audit Plc for non-audit services are not disclosed in the accounts of the Company because such fees are disclosed on a 
consolidated basis for the Group.

During the year exchange gains of £4.4 million were taken to the profit and loss account in respect of US$123.4 million foreign currency 
borrowings, which are treated as a hedging instrument against foreign currency investments. Exchange losses of £4.4 million were taken  
to the profit and loss account in respect of US$123.4 million of foreign currency investments (the hedged item).
Fair values
Under FRS26, all derivative financial instruments not in a hedge relationship are derivatives at fair value through the profit and loss account.  
All transactions in derivative financial instruments are undertaken to manage risks arising from underlying business activities.
For cash, the fair values are the same as the carrying value. For derivative financial instruments, fair values are obtained from the counterparty 
providing the instrument. For floating rate borrowings, fair values have been calculated by discounting the cash flows at appropriate prevailing 
market rates. Other assets and liabilities reflect management’s estimate of value on an appropriate basis.

16 Related parties
The Company has a related party relationship with its subsidiaries, details of which are set out on page 95, and with its Directors and officers. 
Details of the Company’s related party relationships with its Directors are set out in the Remuneration Report. Transactions the Company  
enters into with its subsidiaries, and transactions between subsidiaries, for the sale and purchase of products or services, are priced on an arms 
length basis.

For the year to 31 March 2011 79 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
Non-executive Directors are encouraged to become familiar with  
the Group’s businesses and there is regular communication between 
executive management and Non-executive Directors. The Chairman  
is responsible for ensuring that Board meetings operate to an 
appropriate agenda and that adequate information is provided 
sufficiently in advance of meetings to allow proper consideration.  
He is supported by the Company Secretary, to whom all Directors  
have access. The Company Secretary acts as secretary to the Board  
and audit committee. 
The Board has an agreed procedure for any Director to obtain 
independent professional advice at the Company’s expense. Directors’ 
and officers’ liability insurance is held by the Company and details have 
been circulated to the Directors.
The Board membership and that of its committees is designed to 
ensure that no one individual or group of individuals dominates 
proceedings and that the wide variety of skills allows effective 
leadership across the Group’s business activities. In view of the nature 
of the Group and the details shown in this Corporate Governance 
statement, the Board believes that the current number and balance  
of Directors is appropriate.
The Chairman and Directors regularly discuss matters informally 
outside of Board meetings. In addition, meetings of the Non-executive 
Directors are held annually, both with and without the Chairman being 
present. Such meetings are chaired by the Senior Independent Director.
The Senior Independent Director is responsible for appraising the 
performance of the Chairman and is available to meet shareholders to 
discuss concerns that they may have.
There is a clear division of responsibility between the Chairman  
and Chief Executive, which is reflected in the Board’s Practices and 
Procedures document. In summary, the Chairman is responsible for the 
leadership and running of the Board but does not have any executive 
powers or responsibilities. The Chief Executive leads the executive 
management team in running the Group’s businesses and in 
implementing operating and strategic plans under authority delegated 
by the Board. During the year, the Group’s executive committee was 
comprised of Clive Snowdon, Doug Robertson and Andrew Moss as 
Executive Directors, Mike Giles as Group Operations Finance Director 
and Steve Bowers as Company Secretary.
Standing committees of the Board
The principal standing committees of the Board are the audit 
committee, the remuneration committee and the nomination 
committee. Each of these committees operates under written terms  
of reference which clearly set out their respective delegated 
responsibilities and authorities, copies of which are available from the 
Company Secretary or on the Company’s website www.umeco.com.
Statement of compliance
The Board is firmly committed to ensuring business integrity and  
high ethical values across the Group’s operations. As an essential  
part of this commitment, the Board supports high standards of 
corporate governance and has a policy of seeking to comply with  
the recommendations of the Combined Code (the ‘Code’). Details of 
the mechanisms used by the Company to achieve compliance with  
the Code are shown in this Corporate Governance statement  
and in the Remuneration Report.
The Company was fully compliant with the provisions of the Code 
throughout the year, except that the Company did not have a Senior 
Independent Director from 1 April 2010 until 30 April 2010, when 
Adrian Auer was appointed as a Non-executive Director and new 
Senior Independent Director.
The Board
Following the appointment of Adrian Auer as Non-executive Director 
on 30 April 2010, the Board consisted of eight Directors: five Non-
executive and three Executive. 
During the period from 1 April 2010 to 29 April 2010, the Board 
consisted of seven Directors: four Non-executive and three Executive. 
The names, roles and biographical details of the Directors are set out 
on pages 24 and 25. 
Each of the Non-executive Directors, including the Chairman, is free 
from any business or other relationship which could materially 
interfere with the exercise of his judgement. Each of the Non-executive 
Directors is considered by the Board to be independent.
The Board maintains a Practices and Procedures document which  
sets out the Board’s key administrative processes used to ensure 
information is provided to the Board and its committees to enable 
them to fulfil their roles properly. The Practices and Procedures 
document was updated by the Board in February 2008. The document 
contains the list of matters reserved for the Board which has been 
compiled to ensure that the Board is made aware of all matters that 
are appropriate for it to consider, and has also been communicated to 
the management of the Group’s companies to enable them to manage 
their operations within a clearly defined framework of control. Matters 
reserved for the Board include major investment decisions and changes 
in the composition of the Group. The Board approves the Group’s 
strategic plan, which includes financial and operational objectives, and 
considers detailed financial and operational reports on the progress of 
the Group. Senior executives below Board level are invited to attend 
certain Board meetings to make presentations and participate  
in discussions. Authority has been delegated to the executive 
management team to deal with specific matters, including capital 
expenditure, contract approval, acquisitions and disposals at certain 
levels as determined by the Board.

Disposal of Supply Chain
The disposal of the Supply Chain business has been managed by an independent committee of the Board, established during the year to  
31 March 2011. This committee comprised all Board members other than Clive Snowdon and Doug Robertson. This composition was a 
consequence of Clive Snowdon and Doug Robertson having expressed an interest in participating in a management buy-out of the Supply Chain 
business supported by one of the bidders for the business whose bid was ultimately unsuccessful. The Company is committed to high standards 
of corporate governance and, to ensure no conflicts of interest arose, the independent committee was established with responsibility for all 
matters relating to the disposal process. The independent committee was advised by N M Rothschild & Sons Limited. 
The disposal process has involved the commitment of significant resources to ensure the process and associated risks have been properly 
managed. This has led to the Chairman committing significant additional time to his work with the Group. There have been no changes in the 
Chairman’s external commitments which have affected his ability to perform his role with the Group and Neil Johnson has therefore been able  
to commit a significantly higher proportion of his time to the Group in order to manage and support the disposal process. Neil Johnson is 
chairman of the independent committee and Steve Bowers is secretary to the independent committee.
The independent committee met on 14 occasions during the year to 31 March 2011. Each meeting was fully attended, other than by Stephen Bird 
who attended 11 of the 14 meetings.
Meetings and attendance
The Directors ensure the effectiveness of the Board through the holding of regular Board meetings and by having open lines of communication 
between all Board members. During the year to 31 March 2011, the Board met nine times. The audit committee met on three occasions and  
the remuneration committee met four times. The nomination committee met twice during the year.

Audit committee
The audit committee is chaired by Graham Zacharias. At 31 March 2011, the committee‘s other members are Stephen Bird and Adrian Auer. 
Adrian Auer was appointed a member of the committee on 30 April 2010. Graham Zacharias is a chartered accountant with recent and relevant 
financial experience and Stephen Bird and Adrian Auer are senior business executives who have significant experience of corporate financial 
matters. The members of the audit committee ensure that their knowledge of relevant legislation and best practice developments is maintained. 
The committee received reports from the external auditor who attended the committee’s meetings. The committee also calls upon the Finance 
Director and Company Secretary to attend portions of its meetings. The committee’s work included reviewing the financial statements, 
accounting policies and significant areas of judgement. The committee also assessed the proposed external audit approach and the 
independence and objectivity of the external auditor. In assessing auditor independence the committee obtained confirmation from the external 
auditor that its ethics and independence policies complied with the requirements of the Institute of Chartered Accountants in England and 
Wales. The use of the auditor for non-audit work is monitored by the committee. The Board’s approval is required prior to the Company’s external 
auditor undertaking significant due diligence or similar project-based advisory work for the Group. The Board and audit committee continue to 
believe that there are certain non-audit services where it is more efficient and more cost effective for the external auditor to be used. These 
include conducting financial due diligence in respect of potential acquisition opportunities and vendor due diligence in relation to the disposal  
of the Supply Chain business. Details of the amounts paid to the auditor during the year for audit and other services are set out in note 3 to the 
consolidated financial statements on page 46. During the year, the Company appointed Deloitte LLP as its tax advisor.
Corporate Governance continued  81 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
Nomination committee
The Board recognises the need to refresh its membership and properly 
manage the process by which new Directors are appointed. The 
nomination committee is responsible for identifying and selecting 
candidates to fill Board vacancies for both Executive and Non-
executive positions. The committee also keeps under review the 
structure, size and composition of the Board, to ensure the Board 
continues to have an appropriate balance of skills and experience.  
The committee comprises all members of the Board, other than the 
Director whose replacement is being selected. The Chairman of the 
Company is normally chairman of the committee, other than when  
the Chairman’s replacement is being selected, in which case the  
Senior Independent Director shall chair the committee. 
Where appropriate, the nomination committee uses the services  
of external recruitment consultants. Details of potential candidates 
provided by consultants may be initially reviewed by a sub-committee 
of the nomination committee and meetings with selected candidates 
are then held with Directors. Subsequently, the nomination committee 
meets to discuss and confirm an appointment.
In conjunction with the Company Secretary, the committee will ensure 
that on appointment to the Board, Non-executive Directors receive a 
formal letter of appointment setting out clearly what is expected of 
them in terms of time commitment, including committee service and 
involvement outside Board meetings, and will ensure they receive an 
adequate introduction to the Group and its activities, including site 
visits to the Group’s principal operations. The nomination committee 
also reviews the Company’s succession plans. 
The Board as a whole also considers this subject and considers 
succession planning for senior Corporate executives, with the 
nomination committee focusing specifically on succession planning  
for members of the Board.
The nomination committee met twice during the year. The committee 
met once in relation to the appointment of Adrian Auer as a Director. In 
addition, the committee met in relation to the potential changes in the 
constitution of the Executive Directors resulting from the disposal of the 
Supply Chain business. These meetings were chaired by Neil Johnson.
Investor relations
The Annual General Meeting is recognised by the Board as an 
important opportunity to meet and communicate with shareholders, 
particularly private investors. The 2010 Annual General Meeting  
was held on 28 July 2010 and was chaired by Neil Johnson. The 
meeting was attended by all of the Directors. The Chairman of the 
meeting encouraged debate and questions at the formal meeting and 
informally during refreshments afterwards.
The responsibilities and objectives of the audit committee are set  
out in the committee’s terms of reference, which are summarised  
as follows:
to review the financial statements of the Group and report on • 
matters of significance to the Board, particularly any changes in 
accounting policies and practices, major judgemental areas and 
significant adjustments arising from the external audit;
to be responsible for the appointment, re-appointment and removal • 
of the Company’s external auditor, subject to consultation with the  
Board and shareholder approval, and to oversee the relationship 
with the external auditor;
to review the audit planning process and scope of work performed • 
by the external auditor; and
to review the Company’s internal financial control system and risk • 
management systems and to periodically review the need for an 
internal audit function, unless these have been expressly addressed 
by the Board itself.
An annual assessment of the effectiveness of the Company’s system  
of internal controls was conducted in March 2011. The Board reviewed 
changes in significant risks, the scope and quality of the ongoing 
monitoring of risks, the extent and frequency of the communication  
of the results of the monitoring to the Board and the incidence of 
significant control failings.
Three audit committee meetings were held during the year. These 
considered the results of the interim and full year audit processes,  
and also considered the planning and scope for the auditor’s work  
in respect of these financial statements. 
Remuneration committee
The remuneration committee is chaired by Stephen Bird. The committee’s 
other members are Graham Zacharias and Chris Hole. In order to avoid any 
compromise in the activities of the remuneration committee, the 
chairman of the committee takes responsibility for minuting meetings. 
The committee’s main responsibilities are to determine the specific 
remuneration packages of the Chairman, Executive Directors and 
Company Secretary including salaries, annual bonus and longer term 
incentive schemes, pensions and other benefits. Further information on 
the structure of remuneration implemented by the committee is 
contained in the Remuneration Report, which also contains further details 
of the work of the committee. There is a separate Non-executive Directors’ 
remuneration committee which has responsibility for reviewing the 
remuneration of the Non-executive Directors. The members of the 
Non-executive Directors’ remuneration committee are the Chairman, 
Chief Executive and Finance Director. This committee met four times 
during the year. Until 30 April 2010, there was a separate Chairman’s 
remuneration committee which had responsibility for reviewing the 
remuneration of the Chairman. The Chairman’s remuneration committee 
comprised the Chief Executive, Senior Independent Director and chairman 
of the remuneration committee. This committee met once on 30 April 
2010. Since that date, responsibility for the Chairman’s remuneration has 
been transferred to the remuneration committee.

Each substantially separate issue was put to the 2010 Annual General 
Meeting as an individual motion and the meeting was invited to adopt 
and approve the financial statements and the Directors’ Report for the 
year to 31 March 2010. A separate resolution for the approval of the 
Directors’ Remuneration Report was also put to the meeting. Notice of 
the 2010 Annual General Meeting was sent to shareholders more than 
twenty working days in advance of the meeting and the level of proxy 
votes lodged for and against each resolution, together with details of 
abstentions, were disclosed at the meeting. After the conclusion of 
each Annual General Meeting the results in respect of every resolution 
are published through a Regulatory Information Service and on the 
Company’s website. Full details are also available upon request from 
the Company Secretary. In addition to the Annual Report, the Company 
produces an interim report which is sent to shareholders and publishes 
interim management statements in the second and fourth quarters  
of its financial year. The Group’s website, www.umeco.com, includes 
copies of certain key presentations made by senior management, 
recent annual and interim reports, press releases and links to the 
websites of the Group’s businesses.
The Board as a whole seeks to maintain a thorough understanding of 
the issues and concerns of major shareholders. Dialogue is maintained 
with shareholders and the Executive Directors regularly meet with 
institutional investors. The Chief Executive and Finance Director have 
primary responsibility for investor relations and updates on this subject 
are provided at all Board meetings. In addition, copies of analyst 
research notes and regular reports from the Company’s corporate 
broking advisors are provided to the Board. The Chairman, Senior 
Independent Director and other Non-executive Directors will consider 
requests for meetings with shareholders.
Board induction, development, evaluation and re-appointment
The Company ensures that all new Directors receive a tailored 
introduction to the Group and its activities, including site visits to the 
Group’s principal operations. In addition to the reporting contained in 
papers provided to the Board each month, members of the executive 
committee provide regular input at meetings to help keep the Board 
up-to-date with matters of significance to the Group. Board meetings 
are held at the Group’s principal operating units on a rolling basis, most 
recently in May 2011 at the facilities of Advanced Composites Group in 
Heanor and Non-executive Directors are encouraged to make 
additional visits to the Group’s operations in order to ensure their 
knowledge remains current. The training and continuing professional 
development needs of Directors are kept under review with ongoing 
training being provided as necessary. The Group seeks to ensure that 
the composition of the Board results in Board members having a 
diverse mix of backgrounds, including executive and non-executive 
positions, and with perspectives of relevance to the Group, including 
experience of the Group’s markets, financing and investor experience.
Formal evaluations of the performance of the Board and its 
committees are conducted annually. The most recent evaluation  
was made in March 2011 by the Chairman in conjunction with the 
Company Secretary. The evaluation took into account the views  
of each of the Directors on a wide range of matters, including the 
performance of the Board, its committees and the Directors, and 
matters relating to the leadership and culture of the Group. The  
results of the evaluation process are compiled and summarised by  
the Company Secretary, and then reported to the Board. Where 
required, the Board has then acted in order to enhance further the 
effectiveness of the Board’s procedures and working practices.
Each new appointee to the Board is required to stand for re-appointment 
at the next Annual General Meeting following their appointment. In 
addition, any Director who held office at the time of the two preceding 
Annual General Meetings and who did not retire at either of them, and 
any Non-executive Director who has been in office for a period of nine 
years or more will automatically stand for re-appointment.
The re-appointment of Graham Zacharias, which will be proposed at 
the Annual General Meeting, has been rigorously reviewed by the 
nomination committee. Graham has been a Non-executive Director 
since September 2005.
The Board considers that each of the Directors seeking re-appointment 
at the 2011 Annual General Meeting should be supported by 
shareholders since each of these Directors continues to be effective and 
demonstrates commitment to his role.
Financial reporting
Nature of the Group
The Group has a clear organisational structure and well established 
reporting and control disciplines. Directors of the Group’s operating 
companies assume responsibility for, and exercise a high degree of 
autonomy in, running day-to-day trading activities. These activities  
are conducted within a framework of clear rules, authority limits and 
policies regarding business conduct, which are documented in the 
Group’s Policies & Procedures Manual. The Manual sets out minimum 
standards for accounting systems and controls, and has been made 
available on the Group’s intranet to ensure all appropriate staff have 
ready access to its content. Certified quarterly reports are required 
from operating company management which confirm compliance  
with the Group’s key internal controls.
In view of the devolved nature of the Group, and the disciplines 
referred to above, the Company does not require an extensive  
head office function nor is it appropriate for it to operate with  
a large number of Executive Directors. The Board considers these  
to be commercial strengths for the Group and they have been 
important factors in the Board’s assessment of its Corporate 
Governance arrangements.
Through monthly Board meetings held by each operating company, the 
Executive Directors maintain close and frequent contact with 
operating company management. In addition to financial performance, 
the reporting made by operating companies covers non-financial 
matters, notably health & safety and the environment. The reporting 
includes key performance indicators relevant for each operating 
company. Summaries of the Group’s key performance indicators are 
provided to the Board each month.
Corporate Governance continued  83 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
All operating companies prepare rolling forecasts extending for four 
calendar quarters and a strategic plan, which includes projections for 
the next three financial years. These are reviewed in detail by the 
Executive Directors and are consolidated for review and approval  
by the Board. Performance against forecast is continually monitored  
by the Executive Directors, reviewed at monthly meetings of the 
executive committee and reported to all meetings of the Board.
Systems of internal control
As required by the UK Listing Authority, the Company has complied 
with the Combined Code provisions on internal control. The Company 
has in place risk assessment processes and established procedures 
necessary to implement the Turnbull Committee guidance, as updated 
by the Financial Reporting Council, and for reporting in accordance 
with that guidance.
The Board has overall responsibility for the Group’s system of  
internal control and for reviewing its effectiveness, whilst the role  
of management is to implement Board policies on risk and control.  
The system of internal control is designed to manage rather than 
eliminate the risk of failure to achieve business objectives and can  
only provide reasonable and not absolute assurance against material 
misstatement or loss.
There is a continuous process for identifying, evaluating and managing 
the significant risks faced by the Group, which has been in place for the 
year under review and up to the date of approval of this Annual Report.
The Board has reviewed the effectiveness of the Group’s system of 
internal controls during the year, including strategic, operational,  
legal and compliance, risk management and financial controls. The 
processes used by the Board for their review include the following:
the Board receives regular reports from management which • 
highlight any material control weaknesses and discusses actions 
taken on weaknesses identified by management;
the audit committee, based on reports provided by the external • 
auditor, reviews the effectiveness of the internal financial control 
system, and any significant matters are referred to the Board for 
consideration. The chairman of the audit committee reports the 
outcome of the audit committee meetings to the Board; and 
the Board considers all significant financing and investment • 
opportunities relating to the Group, including the granting of 
guarantees, and monitors policy in respect of managing treasury  
and exchange risks.
Consistent with the Turnbull Committee guidance, the Group’s 
management operated a risk management process during the year 
which identifies the key risks facing each of the Group’s businesses, 
and reports to the Board on how those risks are being addressed. This 
is based on each business producing a report on business development 
policy and a risk register, which identifies the key risks facing the 
business, the probability of those risks occurring and the actions being 
taken to mitigate those risks to the desired level.
These reports are combined to provide the Board with a report of the 
significant risks faced by the Group as a whole, together with details  
of the controls in place over those risks.
Whistleblowing policy
The Group is committed to the highest standards of openness and 
accountability and encourages its members of staff to raise genuine 
concerns about malpractice at the earliest practicable stage rather 
than wait for proof. The Group Policies & Procedures Manual 
encourages concerns to be disclosed, in confidence, orally or in writing, 
to the Group Operations Finance Director or the Company Secretary. 
The Group will take appropriate action against any person victimising 
another for using this procedure or deterring any person from 
reporting genuine concerns under it.
Internal audit
The Group does not have a separate internal audit function, however 
the central finance department conducts detailed reviews of the 
financial records and controls of the Group’s operating companies.  
The results of these reviews are provided to the Board and the external 
auditor. The Board periodically reviews the need for a separate internal 
audit function and has done so during 2011. In light of the reviews 
carried out by the central finance department, the current conclusion  
of the Board is that a separate internal audit function is not necessary.
Through the procedures outlined above, the Board has considered all 
significant aspects of internal control for the year and up to the date  
of this Annual Report. The Board believes that the Group’s system of 
internal control, which is designed to manage rather than eliminate 
risk, provides reasonable but not absolute assurance against material 
misstatement or loss.
Corporate social responsibility
The Board takes account of social, environmental and ethical 
considerations when managing the Group and when considering new 
investment opportunities. This is monitored as part of the Group’s 
annual risk assessment process. The direct environmental impact  
of the Group’s activities is limited, however the Group considers the 
environmental impact of all significant investment opportunities  
and is engaged in a continuing effort to improve the environmental 
performance of all of its businesses. The Group aims to reduce its 
impact on the environment by controlling energy usage, which  
may be achieved by avoiding any unnecessary expenditure,  
improving cost-effectiveness or taking any other appropriate  
steps to reduce energy consumption levels.

Health & safety remains a key component of the Group’s corporate 
social responsibility strategy. Reporting of health & safety matters is 
made to the Board every month. The Group’s health & safety policy 
statement is regularly updated and circulated to the Group’s operating 
companies. Specialist staff at each of these companies ensure 
compliance with this statement. Root cause analysis and similar 
investigative work is carried out following all health & safety incidents. 
The Group maintains accident reporting systems which are primarily 
used to identify trends with a view to developing strategies for 
reducing the number of accidents. There were no major health & 
safety incidents during the year to 31 March 2011.
The Group’s current system of risk management and control, which 
includes social responsibility matters, is led by each of the Group’s 
operations. Senior staff at these companies are responsible for 
complying with the relevant environmental regulations in all the 
geographical areas in which they operate. During the year they 
reported to the Board on such issues through the Chief Operating 
Officer, who has ultimate responsibility for such matters, as part of the 
Group’s system of internal control and risk management reporting. 
Overall the Group continues to believe that its activities have a limited 
environmental impact. However, the Group recognises that it has a 
responsibility to understand the impact that its activities have at local, 
national and global level. These have been monitored and assessed, 
and solutions have been implemented as appropriate according to best 
practice, local legal and other requirements.
The Group continues to focus attention on areas where its impact on 
stakeholders is most beneficial, by delivering an improved and more 
secure environment for our employees, customers and suppliers, and 
by operating ethically as an international Group. The Group’s values 
statements, set out below, are key to the Group’s success and the way 
in which it conducts business:
build with integrity, fairness and trust; • 
challenge and innovate; • 
always put delivery first; and • 
make ambition work. • 
Employment
Employment policies throughout the Group have been established  
to comply with relevant legislation and codes of practice relating  
to employment, health & safety and equal opportunities. The  
Group provides high quality working environments and facilities for 
employees, and training and development appropriate to each of their 
roles. The Group does not discriminate against employees in any way 
and provides a competitive range of employee benefits. The Group 
keeps employees informed on matters relating to their employment 
and on financial and economic factors affecting the Group. This is 
achieved through management briefings, the Group’s website and  
by distribution of press releases and internal announcements. This 
enables employees to gain a better understanding of the Group’s 
business objectives and their roles in achieving them. Building and 
developing the skills, competencies, motivation and teamwork of 
employees is recognised by the Board as being key to achieving the 
Group’s business objectives. The Group places importance on the 
contributions to be made by all employees to the progress of the  
Group and aims to keep them informed by the use of formal and 
informal meetings.
The Group’s commitment to rewarding employees and valuing 
qualities such as determination are enshrined in the Group’s values 
statements. Encouragement is given to all UK employees to participate 
in the Group’s SAYE Share Option Scheme (the ‘Scheme’) under which 
options over the Company’s shares are granted to employees who 
enter into contracts to save agreed amounts each month. The most 
recent invitation under the Scheme was made in July 2009 and further 
invitations are planned.
Ability and aptitude are the determining factors in the selection, 
training, career development and promotion of all employees. The 
Group provides a range of training and development opportunities for 
employees, including induction training, health & safety training and 
support with programmes leading to relevant professional or academic 
qualifications, in addition to specific training related to the role of  
each employee. The Group recognises its responsibility under the UK’s 
Disability Discrimination Act 1995 and does not discriminate against 
disabled people. If an employee is, or becomes, disabled during their 
period of employment, the Group will, if necessary and to the extent 
possible, adapt the working environment to enable the employee to 
continue in their current position or retrain the employee for duties 
suited to their abilities following disablement. It continues to be the 
Group’s policy to consider applications for employment from disabled 
people on the same basis as other potential employees.
Corporate Governance continued  85 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
Health & safety training is part of the induction process for new 
employees. Specific training is given where relevant, for example 
regarding forklift truck operation and chemical handling, as well  
as fire safety and first aid matters.
Risk assessments are used in all parts of the Group, with these  
being updated on a regular basis and also when new equipment  
or machinery is acquired or new processes are introduced.
Going concern
A review of Group business activities and future outlook is set out  
on pages 8 to 23 which includes the Chairman’s Statement, Chief 
Executive’s Review and Finance Director’s Review. The financial 
position of the Group, its cash flows and liquidity position is shown  
in the Consolidated Balance Sheet, Consolidated Statement of Cash 
Flows and accompanying notes to the financial statements. The 
principal business risks associated with the business are shown on 
pages 20 to 22. In addition, note 27 to the consolidated financial 
statements includes the Group’s objectives, policies and processes for 
managing its capital, its financial risk management objectives, details 
of its financial instruments and hedging activities and its exposures to 
credit and liquidity risk. 
The Group’s bank facilities with Lloyd’s Banking Group amount to 
£159.1 million. This comprises a US$150.0 million committed revolving 
facility which extends to June 2014, a US$89.0 million term loan facility 
expiring in August 2012 and an overdraft facility of £10.0 million. 
The Group has entered into an agreement for a new five-year 
committed multi currency revolving credit facility with HSBC Bank plc 
and Santander UK plc, comprising £15.0 million, US$15.0 million and 
US$10.0 million facilities. Utilisation of the facility is conditional on, 
inter alia, completion of the disposal of the Supply Chain business and 
notices of prepayment being delivered to Lloyds Banking Group in 
respect of the facilities referred to above.
After considering the nature and duration of these facilities and 
making appropriate enquiries, based on the strength of the Group’s 
balance sheet, current expectations of future trading (based on future 
cash flow forecasts and revenue projections which the Directors 
believe are based on a realistic assessment of future business 
performance) and on the facilities available to the Group, the Directors 
believe they have reasonable grounds for stating that the Company 
and the Group have adequate resources to continue in operational 
existence for the foreseeable future. For this reason, they continue to 
adopt the going concern basis in preparing the financial statements.
Environment
Umeco operates at the leading edge of environmental change in its 
principal markets, with the Group’s advanced composite materials and 
services being used to improve fuel efficiency and reduce emissions.  
The Group’s customers operate in industries that demand high 
environmental standards from their suppliers and the Group 
continually raises its standards in response. 
Well established environmental management systems and 
comprehensive policies are in place. The Group strives to make 
continuous improvements to its usage of natural resources, in areas 
such as recycling and the efficient use of energy and water. Recycling 
processes have been in use in the Group for many years, and recycled 
materials are used where possible. Improvements to reduce the 
environmental impact of the Group’s operations are regularly 
implemented. Further details are set out on page 23.
Community impact and involvement
The Group encourages employees to support local worthwhile causes 
and charities, and ensures that the Group’s operations cause minimal 
negative impact within the community. In common with all 
companies, the Group has limited resources and the amount of money 
available for charitable purposes varies over time.
Relationships with suppliers, customers and other stakeholders
The Group recognises the obligations it has towards the parties with 
whom it has business dealings including customers, shareholders, 
employees, suppliers and advisors. Dealings with these parties  
depend upon the honesty and integrity of the Group’s staff and every 
effort is made to ensure that a high standard of expertise and business 
principles is maintained in such dealings. Where appropriate, training  
is given to maintain and to raise standards.
The Group’s policy towards suppliers is that each operating company is 
responsible for negotiating the terms and conditions under which they 
trade with suppliers. Once terms are agreed, payments to suppliers are 
made in accordance with those terms and conditions, subject always 
to the supplier having complied with them.

The Remuneration Report is presented to shareholders by the Board 
and sets out the remuneration policy and details of the remuneration 
of each Director in respect of the year to 31 March 2011. The Report 
will be put to the 2011 Annual General Meeting for approval  
by shareholders.
Remuneration committee
The remuneration committee is chaired by Stephen Bird and the 
committee’s other members are Graham Zacharias and Chris Hole.  
The committee has access to the Company’s professional advisors and 
is empowered to seek further independent professional advice if this is 
required. The committee is responsible for all aspects of the 
remuneration packages of the Chairman, the Executive Directors and 
certain other members of senior management. The members of the 
committee have no personal financial interest in the Company, other 
than as shareholders and in respect of the fees received in their 
capacity as Non-executive Directors. They have no day-to-day 
involvement in the management of the Group nor do they have any 
potential conflicts of interest arising from cross-directorships, and they 
do not participate in any form of performance related pay or pension 
arrangements. The Chairman, Chief Executive and Company Secretary 
may attend meetings of the remuneration committee by invitation.  
No Executive Director or other attendee participates in discussions 
relating to their own remuneration.
Remuneration policy
The remuneration policy is set by the Board as a whole with the 
remuneration committee then working within this policy to set 
individual levels of remuneration. The aim of the policy is for the Group 
to attract, motivate and retain high calibre executives by rewarding 
them with competitive salary, benefit and incentive packages which 
are linked to performance and which are designed to enhance the 
business and the creation of shareholder value. The remuneration 
committee uses the services of Deloitte LLP, whom it appoints to 
provide remuneration advice and salary benchmarking data. During 
the year, Deloitte LLP also provided corporate tax advisory services to 
the Group.
During the year to 31 March 2010, the remuneration committee 
reviewed the structure of Executive Directors’ remuneration and 
concluded that changes be made for the year to 31 March 2011 and 
beyond. These changes are designed to strengthen alignment of 
management and shareholder interests, as well as to bring the total 
remuneration package more in line with market practice. These 
changes have been implemented during the year to 31 March 2011  
and comprised: 
the introduction of a Performance Share Plan (‘PSP’), which was • 
approved by shareholders at the Company’s 2010 Annual General 
Meeting. Typically the PSP will operate with an annual award of 50 
per cent of salary in performance shares. It is currently intended 
that, in respect of awards made under the PSP, half will be subject 
to EPS growth targets and half will be subject to relative Total 
Shareholder Return (‘TSR’) performance;
the introduction of a shareholding guideline of 1 x salary for • 
Executive Directors. Holdings of deferred shares will be taken into 
account when determining status against this guideline; and
a reduction in the maximum opportunity under the annual • 
performance related bonus (the ‘Umeco Bonus Plan’) from  
150 per cent of salary to 125 per cent of salary. The amount 
deferred under the Umeco Bonus Plan has been reduced from  
three fifths of the total bonus entitlement to two fifths of the  
total bonus entitlement.
Taken together, the remuneration committee considers that these 
changes in remuneration package for Executive Directors will create 
greater alignment with shareholders interests.
The following sections set out the elements of the remuneration 
package for Executive Directors. Senior managers below Board level 
have similar arrangements.
Basic salaries
The basic salaries of Executive Directors are reviewed annually with 
effect from 1 April, or when a change in the scope of an Executive 
Director’s role occurs. The remuneration committee does not have
a formal positioning policy for basic salary levels as it is aware of the 
issues arising from the setting of salary levels solely by reference to a 
benchmark. Instead, when reviewing salaries, the committee
uses external salary information and also takes into account the 
performance of the Group, the calibre of the individual and their 
contribution to the success of the Group. The committee considers
market data for executives of comparable status and skills in 
companies of similar size and complexity. At the Executive’s choosing 
and subject to the approval of the remuneration committee, salary 
may be converted into additional employer pension contributions.
Benefits in kind
Benefits in kind provided are primarily a fully expensed company car 
and private medical insurance. Directors may choose to forego the 
company car benefit in return for an additional payment of salary,  
such payment being calculated so as to leave the Company no worse 
off from the change.
Annual performance related bonus
Executive Directors participate in the Umeco Bonus Plan. The 
performance targets set under the Umeco Bonus Plan are integrated 
with financial projections, prepared at the start of the year. 
Performance targets are reviewed in detail to ensure that they are 
sufficiently stretching and that they continue to be aligned with the 
Group’s strategy and the creation of shareholder value. Performance 
targets used in respect of the year to 31 March 2011 comprise targets 
in respect of the Group’s adjusted profit before tax (50 per cent of 
total entitlement), the Group’s working capital to sales ratio (25 per 
cent of total entitlement) and personal objectives determined with 
regard to the responsibilities of each Executive Director (25 per cent  
of total entitlement). Certain of the personal objectives include 
financial targets.
Remuneration Report  87 Umeco plc Annual Report 2011
For the year to 31 March 2011, in line with the changes to the structure 
of remuneration referred to earlier, Executive Directors were eligible for 
a maximum award of 125 per cent of basic salary. Three fifths of the 
total value of any award is paid in cash (i.e. up to a maximum of  
75 per cent of basic salary) and the remaining two fifths is delivered  
in the form of a deferred award in the Company’s shares (i.e. up to a 
maximum of 50 per cent of basic salary).
Although awards of deferred shares will have been earned as a result 
of performance in a particular year, full entitlement to these shares is 
deferred, normally until the third anniversary of the award date. An 
Executive Director whose employment ceases during this three year 
period, other than for reasons acceptable to the committee, will forfeit 
their right to the deferred shares. Payments under the Umeco Bonus 
Plan are non-pensionable. Any shares required in respect of these 
deferred share arrangements will be acquired in the market and no 
new shares will be allotted.
PSP
Following shareholder approval at the Company’s 2010 Annual General 
Meeting, Executive Directors will participate in the PSP. Typically, an 
award of 50 per cent of salary will be made annually in performance 
shares under the PSP. It is intended that for initial awards, half of the 
award will be subject to EPS growth targets and half of the award will 
be subject to relative TSR performance against an appropriate 
comparator group, in each case adopting stretching performance 
criteria. Performance against these targets will be assessed over a 
three year period.
Initially, it is intended that the following targets will apply to PSP 
awards:
for the EPS portion, 25 per cent will vest for EPS growth of RPI + 5.0 • 
per cent per annum over the three year performance period and 100 
per cent will vest for EPS growth of RPI + 10.0 per cent per annum 
over the same three year performance period; and
for the TSR portion, 25 per cent will vest for median performance • 
over the three year performance period against the FTSE Industrial 
Goods and Services index and 100 per cent will vest for upper 
quartile performance. 
Straight-line pro-rating will apply for EPS and TSR performance 
between these points.
The PSP enables executives to earn shares in the Company based on 
the achievement of stretching performance conditions. Participation  
in the PSP will be offered to Executive Directors and certain selected 
members of the Group’s senior executive management team. Award 
levels to participants below Executive Director level will be 
appropriately scaled to reflect their role.
It had been intended that the first awards under the PSP would be 
granted in July 2010, immediately following shareholder approval. 
However work ongoing at that date in relation to the disposal of the 
Supply Chain business meant that, following the guidelines of the 
Model Code, the granting of awards at that time was not possible. No 
PSP awards have therefore been made in the year to 31 March 2011. In 
order that executives are not disadvantaged as a result of the delay in 
making the first PSP awards, it is intended that these awards will be 
made following the publication of the Company’s results in respect of 
the year to 31 March 2011. These awards will be structured on the 
same basis as they would have been had the awards been granted in 
July 2010, i.e. they will have a value of 50 per cent of executives salary 
levels at that date and the number of shares comprising the award will 
be calculated using share price levels prevailing at that time. These 
initial awards will include performance targets based upon the three 
year period from 1 April 2010 to 31 March 2013. 
A second grant of PSP awards is intended to be made following 
publication of the Company’s results in respect of the year to  
31 March 2011, and will represent the 2011 grant cycle. These awards 
will be determined based upon 50 per cent of salary at the date of 
grant, using the share price prevailing at that time. These second 
awards will include performance targets in line with the terms set out 
earlier in this report, with these targets being assessed based upon the 
three year period from 1 April 2011 to 31 March 2014.
Under the rules of the PSP , the maximum face value of PSP awards 
granted to a participant in any financial year may not exceed 100 per 
cent of their salary at the date of grant, other than in exceptional 
circumstances as determined by the remuneration committee, in which 
case the maximum would be 150 per cent. The committee considers 
that the delay in granting first awards under the PSP due to the disposal 
of the Supply Chain business represents an exceptional circumstance.
Chairman’s 2010 Share Award Plan (‘SAP’)
At the Company’s 2010 Annual General Meeting, shareholders 
approved the SAP which is a specific share incentive arrangement  
for the Chairman. This new share matching plan is designed to align 
the Chairman’s interests with shareholders and also to incentivise  
him and reward him for superior performance of the Company. The 
remuneration committee consider that the targets are challenging and 
any rewards for the Chairman will thus be linked to material increases 
in shareholder value. Conditional on the Chairman purchasing 50,000 
ordinary shares in the Company (which he has already purchased), he 
will receive a matching share award up to 300,000 shares. In order for 
these shares to vest both a share price condition and a TSR condition 
must be satisfied and he must continue to hold his own shareholding 
and generally remain appointed by the Company until 19 October 
2012, which is the normal vesting date for the award. The award does 
not form part of pensionable earnings. No further similar awards can 
be made under the SAP.
The award will normally vest on 19 October 2012 subject to continued 
appointment, and the satisfaction of the share price and TSR 
performance conditions. The share price condition is that the average 
closing share price over the period of 60 consecutive days ending on 
19 October 2012 exceeds the share price in the table below (‘Share 
Price Condition’):

Share options
Executive options
Executive Directors have been eligible to participate in the Umeco

individuals concerned.
SAYE Share Option Scheme
The Group’s SAYE Share Option Scheme (‘SAYE Scheme’) is open to 
Directors spending at least 25 hours per week on Group business. 
Options under the SAYE Scheme are exercisable during a six month 
period commencing three years from the date of grant.

entitlement into salary, or convert an element of their salary into 
pension contributions. All such conversions are subject to the approval

Clive Snowdon

Doug Robertson
